AMGAN: Attention-Driven Multi-Scale GAN with Complementary
Learning Sub-Network for Generalized Non-Uniform Low-Light Image
Enhancement

A dissertation by
Mr. Pansilu Ashinshana Wijesiri

AMGAN

ABSTRACT

ABSTRACT
Low-light image enhancement is a complex and considerably challenging piece of work, while
the accompaniment of variability in lighting conditions often leads the enhancement towards a
trajectory where the result is either too dark or unevenly illuminated. Current techniques
struggle to produce enhancement results that balance the brightness factor adjustment, detail
preservation, and structural coherency, leading towards over-enhancement or underenhancement, especially in non-uniform lighting scenarios, a challenging edge scenario.
This research proposes a novel attention-driven multi-scale GAN, incorporating a generative
adversarial network (GAN) and a complementary learning sub-network (CLSN) for targeted
brightness and color enhancement while preserving detail and texture, producing a perceptually
coherent enhancement result. The CLSN generates an inverse grey map as attention, guiding
the brightness attention dispersion based on grey values across image channels. The GAN
network is accompanied by the U-Net architecture, extracting multi-scale features utilizing
both the spatial and frequency domains and correspondingly a dual Markov discrimination
targeted discrimination distinctions between the global and local image context. This ensures
the generator network produces a coherent visual and structural enhancement.
The proposed AMGAN method, enhanced with the complementary learning sub-network,
achieved a promising result in low-light image enhancement. The trained model presented
effective brightness and contrast enhancement, with a PSNR of 18.2278, SSIM of 0.4594. The
results demonstrate the potential of AMGAN in achieving the desired brightness factor with
expected details while handling varied distributions of light, accompanied by the GAN.
Keywords: Low-light image enhancement, attention maps, multi-scale feature extraction,
generative adversarial network (GAN), complementary learning sub-network (CLSN).
Subject Descriptors:
Computing methodologies → Artificial intelligence → Computer vision.
Computing methodologies → Machine learning → Machine learning approaches → Markov
decision process.
Computing methodologies → Machine learning → Machine learning approaches → Neural
networks.

ACKNOWLEDGMENT

ACKNOWLEDGMENT
This research project is the culmination of unwavering support from a circle of individuals who
have been inspirational and influential in enabling me to give my utmost throughout this
wonderful journey. Foremost among them stand my loving parents and grandparents, whose
unwavering belief in me and life-long nurturing have shaped the person I am today.
Beyond their foundational influence, I wish to express my deepest gratitude to my
supervisor and module leader, Mr. Guhanathan Poravi, for his relentless support and resolute
guidance throughout the tenure of this project. His mentorship is rooted far beyond the scope
of this module, as he has been a pivotal character from the very inception of this program. His
trust in our potential, coupled with his decisive direction of the student, played a crucial role in
ensuring that this project earned a commendation from both domain and technical experts,
particularly considering the limited timeframe for such depth in execution.
Additionally, would like to express special thanks to Mr. Sampath Wijekoon and Mr.
Devon Wijesinghe for their experience-aligned guidance and for generously offering their time
to provide clarification and insights where necessary during this program. My sincere
appreciation is also extended to all the interviewers, evaluators, and survey participants from
across the globe for providing valuable and insightful feedback during the evaluation process
of this project. Furthermore, I am truly grateful to all the lecturers at the university for their
persistent efforts to produce industry-ready professionals, and to the institutional management
for their timely assistance whenever necessary.
Lastly, I wish to pay my highest respect to a special person who stands for profound,
and one who consistently challenged me to view every obstacle as an achievable and an
opportunity, who never allowed complacency, and who embodied the mindset entitled in this
quote from the enlightened one, “Imagine that every person in the world is enlightened but you.
They are all your teachers, each doing just the right things to help you”.

To all those who contributed to this journey, directly or indirectly - Thank you.

CHAPTER 01: INTRODUCTION

CHAPTER 01: INTRODUCTION
1.1 Chapter overview
This chapter marks the inception through laying the groundwork for research towards LLIE, to
focus on developing a robust approach with an attention-driven multi-scale GAN with a
complementary learning sub-network. It begins with defining the problem in the context of
image processing limitations in complex conditions, as with non-uniform lighting, presenting
a precise problem statement and resonating with the motivation behind this study. An initial
review of existing works will highlight the limitations of the current state-of-the-art, as
overlooked generalizability across diverse lighting, which thereby validate the identified
research gaps. The chapter then defines the contributions towards both the problem and
research domain for detailing advancements towards image enhancement and GAN-based
model performance. Furthermore, core research challenges, research questions to be addressed
at the end, research aim, and SMART-based objectives are delineated.

1.2 Problem domain
1.2.1 Low-light image enhancement
There has been a significant focus on improving low-light images, which often experience
noise, artifacts, chromatic aberration, and detail loss due to insufficient illumination (Han, Xiao
and Yin, 2024). Various approaches have been developed to address these issues (Yang et al.,
2023). Despite advancements, image enhancement remains challenging, and diverse
techniques convert low-illumination inputs into high-quality outputs (T Wang et al., 2024).
Traditional methods utilized image priors and physical model adaptions, i.e. histogram
equalization, Retinex-based, dehazing methods (Hai et al., 2023).
Deep learning (DL), particularly through convolutional neural networks (CNNs), has positively
advanced LLIE, tweaking speed, accuracy, and performance. Traditional Retinex methods
utilizing DL have further optimized LLIE outcomes (Yang et al., 2023). Images being crucial
for other high-level tasks like autonomous driving, semantic segmentation, object and face
detection, and low-light conditions that reduce contrast and detail can severely impair system
performance (Hai et al., 2023; Tang et al., 2024).

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

1

AMGAN

CHAPTER 01: INTRODUCTION

1.2.2 Generative Adversarial Network (GAN)
Brought to light by Goodfellow (2014), generative adversarial networks (GANs) have become
the spotlight in deep learning due to their ability to improve performance in various tasks (Hu,
Yan and Deng, 2022). A GAN consists of two feed-forwards, playing the zero-sum game: the
generator and the discriminator, where the generator learns to produce images that resemble
real data from random inputs, while the discriminator differentiates between real and generated
(fake) images (Hu and Li, 2023; X Wang et al., 2024). GANs, gaining heed for being
particularly effective in image restoration tasks as LLIE (Hu, Yan and Deng, 2022), where the
integration promotes the mitigation of block effects artifacts through the adversarial training
mechanism (X Wang et al., 2024).
1.2.3 Attention mechanism
Attention mechanisms (AMs) are pivotal for advancing LLIE and the general restoration of
images. Modeled resembling human visual perception, AMs focus on key areas in which
improvement is required (Hu, Yan and Deng, 2022). LLIE methods use attention to address
luminance, color, and noise (Hu, Yan and Deng, 2022; Fu et al., 2024). These mechanisms filter
out low-quality data from dark regions and utilize enhanced context from attention maps to
improve the local-global features (Huang et al., 2024; Wang and Jin, 2024). With the extraction
of richer semantic features, AMs refine the mapping from low to normal light, thereby
enhancing detail recovery in images with illumination deficiencies (Wang and Zhang, 2023).
1.2.4 Multi-scale feature extraction
Multi-scale feature extraction (MSFE) is also pivotal for effective LLIE, though the least
focused, leading to deficient generalization, stability and issues like artifacts and color
distortion (Fan et al., 2022). MSFE incorporates both global and local contexts, essential for
enhancing expanded dark areas (Tang et al., 2024). As defined Tang (2024), networks utilizing
large convolutional kernels capture broad spatial relationships yet miss fine details, while small
kernels are the exact opposite. Fusing both features enhances the characteristics of the image.

1.3 Problem definition
Low-light image enhancement (LLIE) is a challenging area in computer vision (CV), with a
focal point to improve visibility and contrast across diverse low-illumination conditions,
including edge cases such as non-uniform lighting and extreme darkness. Driving focus solely
on visibility is scarce, as issues of color distortions, artifacts, and noise also need to be
addressed (Liu et al., 2024). Current LLIE methods often rely on probabilistic models that give
Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

2

AMGAN

CHAPTER 01: INTRODUCTION

priority to overall visual coherence, which can negatively impact the consistency of image
details and result in flawed enhancement of coarse images (Tao et al., 2024).
Deep learning (DL) methods have contributed to significant strides in enhancing contrast and
detail recovery through non-linear fitting and neural networks that are optimized. However,
challenges including color distortions persist and artifacts. Generative Adversarial Networks
(GANs) are promiseable, significantly improving enhancements and eliminating block effects
from the enhanced images (X Wang et al., 2024). Incorporating multi-scale features from both
spatial and frequency domains to solve issues of non-uniform lighting by focusing on image
patches, thereby enhancing overall image quality (Huang et al., 2024; X Wang et al., 2024).
1.3.1 Problem statement
Low-light image enhancement, being a highly researched hot topic, remains challenging in
non-uniform lighting conditions, demanding advanced techniques that integrate an attention
mechanism and multi-scale features from both the spatial and frequency domains for a
generalized, robust low-light image enhancement technique.

1.4 Motivation
The swift advancement of AI and its far-reaching application in domains like autonomous
driving, computational photography, and smart cities underscore the quintessential need for
reliable and LLIE techniques. They are essential for improving the performance of high-level
visual tasks. Developing GAN networks capable of better LLIE is paramount in breeding
dependable systems. As technology continues to evolve, the demand for advanced, reliable
systems will inevitably increase, demanding impactful research in the CV (LLIE) domain.

1.5 Existing work
The table that expands on the existing work that circulates within the problem domain and
potentially affects the research carried out can be found in APPENDIX A.1.

1.6 Research gap
•

Challenges in achieving effective LLIE in non-uniform lighting: Despite the existing
LLIE methods, effective LLIE in non-uniform lighting remains a significant challenge,
regardless, of being a traditional or novel DL method (Zhang et al., 2022; Huang et al.,
2024).

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

3

AMGAN
•

CHAPTER 01: INTRODUCTION

Enhancing dynamic results with advanced AMs and MSFEs: Integrating AM along
with MSFE ameliorates dynamic results beyond traditional attention maps, involving the
multi-scale feature extraction process (Liu et al., 2023; X Wang et al., 2024).

•

Advancing GANs with Complementary Learning Sub-Network: GANs, known for
SOTA performance incorporating adversarial training and integration with a CLSN, closely
resembling vision transformers, is a promising approach (Yang et al., 2023).

•

Improving generalization and robustness in LLIE: Although SOTA methods transcend
in LLIE, further tuning is required to improve their generalization and robustness for
diverse high-level and downstream vision tasks (Huang et al., 2024).

1.7 Contribution to body of knowledge
1.7.1 Contribution to problem domain
Novel DL methods for LLIE leverage the adversarial training mechanism of GANs, which
effectively address block artifacts not overseen by SOTA methods. When combined with a
complementary learning sub-network (CLSN), this network is well-promised in tackling
edge cases in LLIE by standing step ahead of the existing methods (X Wang et al., 2024). This
high-level GAN and CLSN architecture produces enhancements that withstand non-uniform
lighting in low-light images, an issue often overlooked by the SOTAs (Huang et al., 2024).
1.7.2 Contribution to research domain
This research project expands the approach to edge cases of non-uniform light distribution in
low-light images using GANs combined with a CLSN, enhancing images with attention
mechanisms and multi-scale feature extraction methods. GANs are well-recognized for
superior enhancements (Fan et al., 2022, 2022; Hu, Yan and Deng, 2022; Lecert et al., 2023;
Liu et al., 2023; Zhang et al., 2024) when compared to other DL methods (Wang et al., 2020;
Fu et al., 2023; Jia et al., 2023; Liu et al., 2023; Yi et al., 2023), and integration of CLSN,
typically used with transformers, can be fused with GANs to further improve enhancements
and address these edge cases (Yang et al., 2023). The proposed method utilizes AMs and
MSFEs for DL through attention maps and the input map features, meeting requirements often
neglected by SOTA methods (Liu et al., 2023; Wang and Jin, 2024).

1.8 Research challenge
The research aims to advance non-uniform LLIE, using a novel approach with a GAN and a
CLSN, further with AM and MSFE (Liu et al., 2023; Yang et al., 2023; He et al., 2024).

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

4

AMGAN

CHAPTER 01: INTRODUCTION

Low-light image enhancement via deep learning networks – In the rapidly evolving field of
low-light image enhancement (LLIE), the emergence of countless approaches with differing
complexities and outcomes presents a challenge. Understanding and adaptively identifying the
most relevant and impactful techniques is crucial (Tang et al., 2024).
Generative Adversarial Networks – GANs, based on the zero-sum game theory (Goodfellow
et al., 2014; Hu and Li, 2023), encounter challenges such as non-convergence and model
collapse during the training phase. Addressing these roadblocks is quintessential for further
incorporating the GAN-based approach in LLIE (Tang et al., 2024).
Complementary Learning Sub-Network – Integrating a learning network to reinforce the
GAN involves vivid experimentations and precise design, producing robust, enhanced images.
Balancing with the capabilities of GAN is a significant challenge (Yang et al., 2023).
Attention Mechanism – Meeting the requirements of varying illumination scenarios with well
and deficiently illuminated regions demands a better dynamic approach (Singh and Parihar,
2024). Time-sensitive integration with precision of multi-dimensional information from both
the spatial and channel domains is committed (Wang and Zhang, 2023).
Multi-Stage Feature Extraction – Balancing global-local illumination utilizing multi-scale
features is challenging (He et al., 2024). Precise extractions from multi-domains, requiring UNet architecture experimentations, essential for effective LLIE (Xu, Wang and Lu, 2023).
Generalization and robustness in diverse environments – Addressing crucial, overlooked
LLIE in heterogeneous environments with diverse, edge-lighting conditions expect models that
are both generalized and robust (Huang et al., 2024; Liu et al., 2024).

1.9 Research questions
RQ1: In what ways can the integration of a Complementary Learning Sub-Network (CLSN)
improve the GAN-based model performance for non-uniform low-light image enhancement?
RQ2: What strategies enable the attention mechanism and GAN-based network integration to
enhance brightness factor uniformity in low-light images persistent with non-uniform lighting?
RQ3: What is the influential impact (in detail and color context) of a multi-scale feature
extraction mechanism on enhancing low-light images in non-uniform lighting conditions?
RQ4: In what ways can the GAN-based networks be directed to produce robust and generalized
enhancements across a diverse non-uniformity range of low-light scenes?
Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

5

AMGAN

CHAPTER 01: INTRODUCTION

1.10 Research aim
This research project aims to design, develop, and evaluate a generalized (i.e. with inclusivity
of non-uniform light scenarios), and robust low-light image enhancement Generative
Adversarial Network architecture with a complementary learning sub-network utilizing
attention mechanism and multi-stage feature extraction.
To further elaborate, the focus of this project will be centered around the development process
of a GAN-based model embodying a reinforcement branch (CLSN), with the contemplation to
produce enhancement results utilizing the AMs accompanied to drive the required focus in the
enhancement process based on the intensity weights of the image patches distributed in the
map and MSFE to explore deep under-explored information in the low-light image. The
approach seeks high quality and improved generalization for LLIE in edge lighting scenarios.

CHAPTER 02: LITERATURE REVIEW

CHAPTER 02: LITERATURE REVIEW
2.1 Chapter overview
This chapter provides a comprehensive review of research circulating in the low-light image
enhancement (LLIE) domain, resonating with the challenges posed by non-uniform lighting
conditions and their impact on varied downstream CV tasks. It critically examines traditional
and state-of-the-art techniques, emphasizing DL methods such as Generative Adversarial
Networks (GANs), multi-scale feature extraction, and attention mechanisms. This chapter also
explores the integration of Complementary Learning Sub-networks (CLSN) into LLIE.
Additionally, the review of evaluation metrics was utilized to assess LLIE methods and
benchmark performances. In addressing the identified gaps and limitations of the existing
approaches, this literature review sets the groundwork for the proposed architecture, thereby
providing a foundation for the methodology discussed in later chapters.

2.2 Concept map
A concept map was constructed to visualize the key concepts, methods, and relationships within
the LLIE domain, particularly with a focus on non-uniform lighting conditions. This map was
designed to ensure that all areas of the problem domain, exciting work, technologies, evaluation
methods, and limitations with relevancy are systematically and panoramically covered in the
literature review. The complete concept map can be found in APPENDIX B.1.

2.3 Problem domain
2.3.1 Significance of LLIE
Low-Light Image Enhancement (LLIE) has been identified as immensely important in
capturing high-quality images in the presence of diverse lighting conditions, ranging from
night-time outdoors to artificially lit indoor and complex edge lighting scenarios (Lecert et al.,
2023; Huang et al., 2024). LLIE has a fixed focal point in improving visibility, contrast, and
reduction of noise, thereby enhancing the CV application performance, which solely relies on
degraded images (L Wang et al., 2024).
In autonomous driving, LLIE plays a significant role (evidently depicted in the figure
below) by allowing the visual sensors to detect road conditions, obstacles, and pedestrians
accurately, especially under interfered visibility conditions, thereby enhancing safety and
system performance (Han et al., 2023; Tan et al., 2023; L Wang et al., 2024). Furthermore,
Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

9

AMGAN

CHAPTER 02: LITERATURE REVIEW

surveillance systems, being another LLIE benefitted candidate, such enhanced image quality
subsequently boosts facial recognition and activity monitoring accuracy in dimly lit
environments (YU, LI and HUA, 2023; Tao et al., 2024). Moreover, in challenge-based
consumer photography performances, as in concert and night-time situations, LLIE contributes
distinctly (Tian et al., 2023).

Figure 1: A sample test image from the ExDark dataset, with the YOLOv4 object detection results on the original and the
enhanced image result produced by (Han, Zhou and Zeng, 2023), on the impact of LLIE in increasing detection accuracy.

In contributions, LLIE plays a notable role in other downstream CV tasks like object detection,
semantic segmentation, and target tracking through model training utilizing enhanced lowillumination images, containing more discernible features and reduced noise (YU, LI and HUA,
2023; Zhang, Wu, et al., 2023; Zhang, Zhou, et al., 2023; Zhou et al., 2023; J Liu et al., 2024;
Ma et al., 2024; Tao et al., 2024). Such vivid applicability underscores the role of LLIE in the
advancement of the CV field (Hu, Yan and Deng, 2022; Hu and Li, 2023; Jin et al., 2023).
2.3.2 Challenges of low-light imaging
Low-light imaging presents a distinctly non-negligible group of challenges, thereby impacting
the quality and usability of images. Below is a breakdown of the key factors in criticalities.
•

High noise levels: The presence of low illumination leads to image captures with high noise
levels due to reduced signal-to-noise ratio (SNR), thereby obscuring the details and causing
graininess in images, which is particularly problematic in precision-driven applications like
medical imaging (Jin et al., 2023; Yao et al., 2024). Therefore, the utilization of advanced
noise reduction techniques is quintessential for balanced clarity and retaining details (Fang
et al., 2024; Jize Zhang et al., 2024).

•

Low contrast: Here, the presence leads to the blending of scene objects into the
background, thereby complicating the object clarity, and affecting tasks like surveillance
facial detection (Han et al., 2023; Shang et al., 2024). With the enhancement process of

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

10

AMGAN

CHAPTER 02: LITERATURE REVIEW

traditional methods, overexposure of bright areas or counter-opposite occurs, resulting in
object clarity complications, highlighting contrast factor importance (Fang et al., 2024).
•

Color distortion: A commonly identified issue in LLIE arises from the uneven color
representations, moreover, specific to under-illuminated regions of the image, causing
overly saturated or unnatural color combinations in the enhanced sections of the image (Lin
et al., 2023; Fang et al., 2024; Xiang et al., 2024).

•

Loss of detail and texture: The majority of the to-date proposed LLIE techniques tend to
overlook the detail and texture preservation factor, which holds considerable weight in
producing better results, critical in CV tasks like feature extraction and recognition, leads
to blurred or lost information, as left unseen (Fan et al., 2023; Fu et al., 2024). Therefore,
such overlooking leads to impaired method effectiveness, particularly in tasks such as
segmentation and classification, which critically utilize such components (T Wang et al.,
2024; Yuan et al., 2024).

•

Dynamic range: The scarce dynamic range in low-light images presents a challenge,
particularly in brightness adjustments, as of non-sacrificing the critical contextual
information in the ill-illumination or well-illuminated regions of the degraded image (Fan
et al., 2023; K-F Yang et al., 2023). Traditional methods have a higher tendency to produce
overexposed or underexposed results, mainly due to the underperformance in controlling
the range dynamically (Guo et al., 2020).

•

Naturalness: Achieving a balance between the enhancement result and maintaining the
naturalness of the image is a critically important goal. Thereby, over-enhancement leads to
the production of unrealistic effects or artifacts, which diminishes both the aesthetic and
practical value of the image (Hu, Yan and Deng, 2022; Hai, Hao, et al., 2023).
Therefore, as per the image to be appraised as reliable and effective, LLIE methods must

competently handle such issues, ensuring practicality and visual consistency, and aligning with
real-world conditions (Chen, Li and Hua, 2023; Han, Zhou and Zeng, 2023; Zhou et al., 2024).
2.3.3 Non-uniform lighting issues
Due to the imbalance in the presence of well-illuminated regions of an image, non-uniform
lighting in low-light environments presents a significant challenge. At the same time, the rest
of the regions remain in the shadow, thereby generating brightness pockets and underexposed
regions. As with the persistence of such edge lighting scenarios, traditional methods tend to
encounter complications, leading to the inability to balance the illumination properly (Khan et
al., 2024; Zhou et al., 2024). Examples of such scenarios range from outdoor night scenes,

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

11

AMGAN

CHAPTER 02: LITERATURE REVIEW

indoor settings with diverse artificial lighting sources, and sunset scenarios, where the
discrepancy between the well-lit and vice-versa often leads to overexposure and loss of
important image details, distributed within the degraded input image (YU, LI and HUA, 2023;
Cao et al., 2024; Yao et al., 2024).

2.3.4 Proposed architecture

Figure 3: Overview of the proposed architecture (self-composed).

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

12

AMGAN

CHAPTER 02: LITERATURE REVIEW

The proposed architecture presented in this section is embedded with a focal point in tackling
the challenges of LLIE, especially towards the existing deficiencies of SOTAs in handling nonuniform lighting. Here, the overall network architecture accompanies a unique measure of
inter-combining the attention mechanism and multi-scale (spatial and frequency domain)
feature utilization based on a U-Net-based GAN with skip connections in the candid
achievement process.
2.3.4.1 Preprocessing phase and attention mechanism
To reduce the computational complexity and enable better convergence during training, a
preprocessing role is accompanied. Before feeding the image into the enhancement pipeline,
the degraded image is resized to 256x256 resolution to meet the aforementioned goal.
Then, an inverse illumination map is generated with the assistance of an AM, which refines
the brightness component, consequently brightening the darker regions and leaving the well-lit
as it is (Fan et al., 2022). After the process is completed, the generator map is concatenated
with the degraded input image to provide a better, information-retained input for the GAN
network.
2.3.4.2 Feature extraction and multi-scale utilization
Reaching the GAN, the proposed architecture employs MSFE with a vision on capturing both
the global and local context and fine details of the image. Leveraging the FFT, the model will
utilize the spatial and frequency domain information for an effective enhancement effect. As,
•

Frequency domain extracts high-frequency components (i.e., edges and texture), crucial
for enhancing the structural integrity and details of the degraded image.

•

Spatial domain, commonly utilized in the majority of the SOTAs, is accompanied to
enhance the color and other general image quality attributes for better enhancement.

2.3.4.3 U-net-based GAN architecture
The GAN generator network, in which the MSFE process is accompanied, is designed based
on the U-Net architecture. The encoder-decoder structure of a U-Net enables the incorporation
of skip connections, thereby targeting minimal information loss during the down-/up-sampling
stages, retaining the critical image feature during the enhancement.
2.3.4.4 Dual Markov discriminator network
The adversarial network which tries to distinctly differentiate the fake and normal images, is
taken a step further incorporating a dual Markov discriminator, evaluating both the local (in
Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

13

AMGAN

CHAPTER 02: LITERATURE REVIEW

patches) and global (the full image) features, ensuring structural precision, additionally (Yu,
Zhao and Zhong, 2023).
•

Local discrimination focuses on specific regions of the image evaluating finer details

•

Global discrimination, in a wider context, examines the overall structural coherence.

Figure 4: Systematic representation of a dual Markov discriminator network (Yu, Zhao and Zhong, 2023).

2.3.4.5 Optimization and loss functions
The model assisted with the Adam Optimizer (Kingma and Ba, 2017) during the training phase
for concise and efficient convergence and additionally incorporates loss functions such as
Adversarial Loss, Perceptual Loss, and Structural Similarity Loss, enabling not only pleasing
enhancements but also the truest version of the content of the original image.
The above-proposed architecture, which accompanies pre-processing towards training
efficiently, attention to U-Net-assisted multi-scale feature utilization, and dual-discrimination,
ensures the aspects of higher quality companying both local and global context of the image.

2.4 Technological review
2.4.1 Review of deep learning techniques
2.4.1.1 Convolutional Neural Networks (CNNs)
Convolutional Neural Networks (CNNs) are fundamental DL architectures widely utilized in
image processing tasks, in the focus of research, the LLIE prospects (Khan et al., 2024).

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

14

AMGAN

CHAPTER 02: LITERATURE REVIEW

2.4.1.1.2 CNNs in LLIE
In LLIE, by learning complex mappings from low light to well-lit images using a supervised
paradigm, CNNs have been able to demonstrate remarkable performance. The focus on
improving the brightness, color, and structure of the image through feature extraction at diverse
scales, thereby increasing the effectivity in the image enhancement process, is to be resonated
(Fang et al., 2024).
CNN-based models like LLNet (Lore, Akintayo and Sarkar, 2017) and LLCNN (Tao et
al., 2017) follow techniques of incorporating stacked sparse denoising autoencoders and
residual networks towards improving contrast and denoising, yet, not required to undergo any
pre- or post-processing measures, and the multi-scale feature extraction across CLs, preserving
the key detailed information in the image, thereby demonstrating the capabilities of CNNs
(Tian et al., 2023).
However, as CNNs have an increased tendency to lack global context awareness and
require a substantial amount of data to avoid instances of overfitting during the model training
phase, it is considered challenging (Fang et al., 2024). Therefore, to address these persisting
issues, hybrid models with attention mechanisms or incorporation of Retinal theory are being
explored, to enhance performance in complex lighting conditions (Hai, Hao, et al., 2023).
2.4.1.1.1 Architectural breakdown of CNNs
The CNN architecture is typically comprised of three key components, each performing in their
respective arena, analyzed as,
i.

Convolutional layers, utilized as the primary feature extraction component, use kernels or
filters to scan the image, thereby extracting local features such as edges, textures, and
patterns, which is crucial in capturing hierarchies in image data (Tian et al., 2023).

ii.

Pooling layers, are solely responsible for spatial dimensionality reduction of the extracted
feature maps, thereby decreasing the computation load and preventing the cause of
situations of model overfitting by retaining only the most significant features. Max-pooling
is a common choice in this aspect of dimension reduction (Hai, Hao, et al., 2023).

iii.

Fully connected layers (dense layers), combine the extracted features of the previous layer
in generating the results, typically in the presence of classification or regression tasks. In
the context of LLIE, FCLs are utilized for the synthesis of enhanced images based on
learning the mapping from low-light inputs (Tian et al., 2023).

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

15

AMGAN

CHAPTER 02: LITERATURE REVIEW

Although these CNNs are very effective in capturing local features, the global context is
often overlooked. This is due to the fixed kernel size in a single convolution operation, which
requires additional measures to increase the receptive field (L Wang et al., 2024), thereby
increasing the tendency of lacking natural global coherence in the enhancement (Tian et al.,
2023).
2.4.1.2 Generative Adversarial Networks (GANs)
2.4.1.2.1 Architectural breakdown of GANs
In the essence of improving image quality, GANs follow a competitive process resembling the
zero-sum game, which involves two main components: a generator and a discriminator. Here,
the generator creates real-like pseudo-images with a focus on deceiving the discriminator,
which utilizes energy to differentiate the distinction between real and synthetic images. This
process continuously iterates until the discriminator is no longer able to demonstrate the
distinction between the two inputs (Tian et al., 2023). The GAN method can be mathematically
described as,

2.4.1.2.2 GANs in LLIE
U-Net-based GAN architectures, utilized for image-to-image translations, as also in Pixe2Pixe
GANs (Singh et al., 2022), gained significant traction due to the feature extraction capabilities
from both the global and local contexts and with the enablement of utilizing skip connections
in retaining the highest information (T Wang et al., 2024; Zhou et al., 2024). EnlightenGAN
Jiang et al. (2021) also utilizes U-Net as the generator to enhance the global brightness and
local details, additionally employing the dual-discriminator. Despite the employments, the
method demonstrates a tendency towards color distortions and noise (Han, Zhou and Zeng,
2023), which is addressable with the incorporation of different measures of attention and
feature extraction, contributing to the overall perceptual quality.

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

AMGAN

CHAPTER 02: LITERATURE REVIEW

CycleGAN is another prominent technique designed to perform the CV task with
unpaired training data with the additional employment of a cycle consistency loss, thereby
ensuring the presence of original content in the generated result (Tang et al., 2024). Although
CycleGAN is recognized as effective in enhancing the overall contrast and brightness of the
degraded image, the retention of texture details is often overlooked, which creates room for
artifacts in complex low-light scenarios (Han, Zhou and Zeng, 2023).
In addressing such issues of recovering fine details and balancing the brightness factor
in the enhanced outcome, with the identification of the potential, U-Net-based architectures are
utilized as room for enabling better spatial relationships, capturing and avoiding the loss of
critical information during the enhancement is denoted capable (Tang et al., 2024).
2.4.1.2.3 Role of Single and Dual Adversarial Networks
•

Single discriminator: Reflecting on a standard adversarial network, utilizing singlephased discriminators, with a focus on evaluating the global characteristics of an image
under the enhancement process. Yet, such a focus only on the global context of the image
and the inability to capture and refine the minute details of the image will direct the result
in an under-enhancement in the local context (L Wang et al., 2024).

•

Dual Markov discriminator: Inspired by EnlightenGAN by Jiang et al. (2021), and
recognizing the limitations of a single discriminator approach, methods have utilized the
dual-discriminator adversarial approach, which consists of a global discriminator for the
entire image, thereby moving focus on the global-context discrimination, while the
commonly

recommended

patch-based

discrimination

for

local-context

driven

enhancements for detail refinement, making it a pinnacle candidate for LLIE tasks,
particularly with non-uniform lighting (Jiang et al., 2021; Fang et al., 2024).
2.4.2 Review of multi-scale feature extraction techniques
2.4.2.1 Pyramid-based techniques
Pyramid-based techniques leverage multi-scale feature representations, capturing both the
global and local features, which is immensely influential in a better enhancement performance.
Following a progressive down-sampling of images in a coarse-to-fine measure, these
techniques make sure that the details of diverse scales are enhanced, while subsequently
maintaining the global consistency (Jin et al., 2023).

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

17

AMGAN

CHAPTER 02: LITERATURE REVIEW

Pyramid structures, such as the Laplacian pyramid, are mainly integrated into GANs
focused on improving the illumination factor of the image across varying resolutions (Lin et
al., 2023).
2.4.2.2 Dilated convolutions
Dilated convolutions, a technique with the capability of expanding the receptive field without
incorporating any additional network parameters, is a potential candidate for multi-scale
contextual feature extraction from degraded inputs in the LLIE task. Such a technique resonates
with the practice of employing multiple dilated convolution layers with varying dilation rates
where the network receives the ability to adaptively incorporate broader features, subsequently
retaining fine details, which is the pivotal role in the LLIE process (Hu, Yan and Deng, 2022;
Hai, Hao, et al., 2023).
2.4.2.3 Wavelet-based and fast-Fourier transform techniques
Wavelet-based techniques decompose images into low and high-frequency components,
thereby enabling the network to precisely lay control of the illumination and details during the
enhancement process. The technique is highly effective, as it maintains the structural
information during the enhancement process, through individual manipulation of the high- and
low-frequency components, and simultaneously reduces the noise that is brought to light, while
improving the overall contrast of the image, which makes it an ideal choice for fine-grained
LLIE (Xiang et al., 2024).
The Fast-Fourier Transform (FFT) technique redeems a close resemblance to the former
technique, as both follow the steps of analyzing the frequency component, with distinct
approaches, which are native to themselves, driven towards one goal. While Wavelet Transform
provides a localized frequency analysis, including both the time and frequency information,
FFT utilizes global frequency analysis across the entire signal, making it an efficient, stand-out
choice for stationary signals, where the counter-opposite is the former technique. While both
complement the main network with multi-scale feature extractions, in summary, the FFT
approach brings a wide, efficient frequency analysis to the table (Jialiang Zhang et al., 2024).
2.4.3 Review of attention mechanisms
Attention, first appearing in (Vaswani et al., 2017), in CV, is a pivotal retrospective that enables
the enhancing ability of the model by directing attention towards the regions or aspects that
dwell with important features, as in the research focus, during the LLIE process. By
incorporating such measures of directing focus towards spatial regions or feature channels,
Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

18

AMGAN

CHAPTER 02: LITERATURE REVIEW

through the approaches of spatial, channel, and multi-head attention, AMs contribute
immensely to detail preservation and context awareness, impacting critically (Cao et al., 2024).
•

Spatial attention, known for prioritizing important regions within an image, utilizes the
generated attention maps, which highlight the areas requiring further attention. In this
mechanism, pooling operations step in to extract spatially significant information, which
consequently enables the model to enhance critical features, driving the least attention
towards mere important regions (Hu and Li, 2023).

•

Channel attention drives focus on relationships of diverse channels of a specific feature
map, thereby enabling the model to recognize the key channels while suppressing mere
importance resonating channels. Global Average Pooling (GAP) with convolutional layer
and activation functions contributes to dynamically recalibrating the feature maps,
subsequently ensuring the retaining of crucial details of the input image (Hu, Yan and Deng,
2022; Fang et al., 2024).

•

Multi-head self-attention enables the capturing of long-range dependencies within an
image. As honey to ears, the enhancement expands to various regions of the feature map,
yet the high computational complexity is nothing short of this method (Zhang et al., 2022).

2.5 Existing work
LLIE techniques, to date, have evolved significantly, addressing the quintessential requirement
of capturing and improving the images in inadequately illuminated conditions (Wang and Jin,
2024). The enhancement methods presented can be broadly categorized into traditional and
modern deep-learning methods, as briefed with a critical comparison below.
2.5.1 Traditional methods for LLIE
2.5.1.1 Histogram equalization and gamma correction methods
Histogram equalization (HE), including global (GHE) and local (LHE) variations, enhances
the image contrast by redistributing the image brightness while stretching the dynamic range
of the image (Kim, 1997; Jin et al., 2023). GHE proceeds to adjust the overall brightness yet
leads to detail over-enhancement, while LHE targets local areas to overcome the limitations
presented by GHE (Kim, Kim and Hwang, 2001; Gonzalez, 2008). Advanced iterations of HE
methods, such as bi-histogram and edge-enhanced double histogram equalization, refine the
brightness and quality a step further (Wang, Chen and Zhang, 1999; Kim, Kim and Hwang,
2001). Despite the demonstrations, these methods tend to amplify noise and create definitive

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

19

AMGAN

CHAPTER 02: LITERATURE REVIEW

visual inconsistencies in edge scenes as non-uniform lighting (Hu, Yan and Deng, 2022; Hai,
Hao, et al., 2023; Jin et al., 2023; Jialiang Zhang et al., 2024).
Gamma correction (GC) adjusts the luminance values to enhance the underlit images,
yet the produced results consist of unnatural color distributions and overexposure in highcontrast regions. (Huang, Cheng and Chiu, 2013; Khan et al., 2024)
However, both the techniques of HE and GC, providing a solid foundation in maturity,
still struggle to retain naturalness in complex lighting scenarios. (Han et al., 2023)
2.5.1.2 Retinex-based methods
Retinex theory, widely utilized in the LLIE domain, is initially proposed by Land and McCann
(1971), is recognized due to the perception modeling ability of two distinct components,
illumination and reflectance, based on the HVS. The Retinex-based methods decompose the
image (I ∈ ℝHxWx3) into reflectance (R ∈ ℝHxWx3), the intrinsic object property, and illumination
(L ∈ ℝHxWx1), the varying lighting condition. (Han, Zhou and Zeng, 2023)
I=R⊙L
Where, ⊙ denotes the element-wise multiplication between the two components, thereby
reconstructing the image, under the corruption-free assumption (Cai et al., 2023). A notable
utilization of this theory by Guo, Li and Ling (2017) refine the initial illumination map by
imposing a structure prior, enabling lighting detail optimization, effectively. Similarly, Fu et al.
(2016) with a weighted variational model, an alternating minimization algorithm is applied to
estimate both components.

Furthermore, Li et al., (2018), predicted a noise map utilizing

Retinex. However, such methods, often struggle to alleviate noise artifacts and produce
accurate color distributions, limiting the ability to handle complex noise and color distortions
in challenging LLIE conditions. (Guo, Li and Ling, 2017; M Li et al., 2018)
2.5.2 Deep learning methods
2.5.2.1 Supervised learning methods
Learning the low-light and counterpart mapping, through extensive training, produces accurate
mappings, yet is limited due to data dependency as discussed. (Zhu et al., 2024)
2.5.2.1.1 End-to-end learning models
End-to-end learning models, notably accompanying deep CNNs, have gained traction due to
the straightforward architecture of supporting the direct mapping from low-light images to their

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

20

AMGAN

CHAPTER 02: LITERATURE REVIEW

counterparts (Tang et al., 2023). Initial contributions include LLNet, accompanying a stacked
denoising autoencoder for brightness enhancement and denoising simultaneously (Lore,
Akintayo and Sarkar, 2017). Subsequently, developments advanced to multi-branch
architecture, such as MBLLEN, providing LLIE integrating feature extraction, enhancement,
and fusion modules (Lv et al., 2018). Recent iterations such as EnGAN (Jiang et al., 2021),
KinD++ (Zhang et al., 2021), and CSDNet (Ma et al., 2022) pushed the boundaries of end-toend enhancements. Despite the possibilities, these models often lack constraints on image
gradients, causing loss of fine details, especially in under-lit regions (Rana, Lal and Parihar,
2021). Earlier to edge-map predictions and Sobel filters, noise and detail loss were advertent,
resulting in unbalanced exposure and color. (M Zhu et al., 2020; Li, Wang and Zhang, 2023)
2.5.2.1.2 Physical interpretable models
Retinex-based techniques, combining physical principles and a supervised learning paradigm,
aim at LLIE while providing interactable results (K-F Yang et al., 2023). Retinex-Net (Wei et
al., 2018) focused on recovering details in the dark but with an increased tendency towards
resulting chromatic aberration, thereby hindering color accuracy. KinD method addressed the
color issue with multiple loss functions, yet resulted in blurred image edges ,(Zhang, Zhang

and Guo, 2019). Merging CNNs with the Retinex theory accompanying multiple scales, MSRNet, underperformed in extreme low-light conditions (Shen et al., 2017). Furthermore,
advancements as, LightenNet and URetinex-Net with the same aim, struggled with overenhancement and artifact generation due to inaccurate illumination estimations, a common
issue of Retinex-theory-based methods (C Li et al., 2018; Wu et al., 2022). Despite the
advancements, chromatic aberrations, edge blurring, and inaccurate illumination estimations
remain challenging, thereby underscoring critical research requirements (Zhao et al., 2022).
2.5.2.2 Unsupervised learning
As the paired low-/normal-light image collection cost is high, and due to the heavy manual
labor intervention, the unsupervised paradigm is brought to light, thereby eliminating data
dependency to an extent, utilizing loss terms. (Yu, Zhao and Zhong, 2023; Song et al., 2024)
2.5.2.2.1 Generative Adversarial Networks
Generative Adversarial Networks (GANs) have significantly contributed to LLIE by producing
robust and generalizable image enhancement techniques (Tang et al., 2024). A GAN-based
method by L Wang et al. (2024) accompanies multi-scale feature extraction, illumination
attention, and an encoder-decoder setup with dual discrimination refining the generator results
with a specialized loss function for maximum color distortion alleviation. However, due to
model complexity and overfitting, and with synthetic training data lacking the expected depth
in comparison to real images, there remain challenges (Jize Zhang et al., 2024). Furthermore,
Jin et al., (2023) employs a dual-branch GAN, which merges gradient learning from event
streams with LLIE, integrated through an attention-based fusion module. Yet the method
remains computationally complex and is restricted to handling grey-scale formats. Resonating
with hybrid attention within a residual module, and capturing multi-scale information for
enhancing details and color accuracy, Yu, Zhao and Zhong (2023) still requires further
optimizations in meeting the ground-truth resemblance.
CycleGAN architecture, another GAN candidate, demonstrates unsupervised based
advancements, which enhance perceptual quality and light essence capture with guided
filtering and joint training strategies aiming at a natural resultant image, but the requirement of
a lightweight version remains unfulfilled (Tang et al., 2024). Meanwhile, dual-branch fusion
by Han, Zhou and Zeng (2023) for noise suppression and global consistency tends to require
further optimization of information processing, especially, temporal and spatial.

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

22

AMGAN

CHAPTER 02: LITERATURE REVIEW

2.5.2.2.2 Zero-shot learning methods
Zero-shot learning methods in LLIE alleviate the reliance on large datasets, with the dynamic
adjustment of image-specific properties without any data (S Yang et al., 2023; L Wang et al.,
2024). Zero-DCE++ (Li, Guo and Loy, 2022), an advanced iteration of Zero-DCE (Guo et al.,
2020) with the limitation of noise amplification and color biases, addresses the issues, yet still
suffers from overexposure and haze artifacts in HDR scenes. Similarly, RRNet by A Zhu et al.
(2020) demonstrated effective denoising yet underperforms in brightness factor enhancements.
Such weaknesses of noise amplification, color inaccuracy, and inadequate exposure, limit the
applicability and broader context, requiring generalization.
2.5.2.3 Vision transformers and other techniques in LLIE
Vision Transformers (ViTs), initially proposed in (Vaswani et al., 2017), for NLP tasks, have
made strides in LLIE through leveraging the self-attention mechanism for capturing long-range
dependencies. Despite the capabilities, resonating on the quadratic computational complexity
and appearance of visible seams in images due to patch-assisted processing during the
enhancement (Cai et al., 2023). Despite the promising outcomes, models like Illumination
Adaptive Transformer (IAT) (Cui et al., 2022) and LLFormer (T Wang et al., 2024) struggle
with pixel-level feature extraction in extreme low-light conditions. And inevitably,
Transformers suffer from subtle artifacts and noise, thereby demonstrating further optimization
requirements to handle variable lighting and fine details (Wang and Jin, 2024).
2.5.3 Multi-scale feature extraction
2.5.3.1 Spatial, frequency, and channel domain information utilization
Multi-Scale Feature Extraction (MSFE) thrives in the LLIE field, leveraging spatial, channel,
and frequency domain information. Utilizing the spatial domain, the MSATr method enhances
the brightness and detail extraction through a multi-scale window division mechanism, yet
balancing complex attention computations for varying lighting conditions remains an active
challenge (Fang et al., 2024). Meanwhile, LEGAN (Fu et al., 2022) and MBLLEN (Lv et al.,
2018) face limitations in preserving details despite the integration of attention and multi-branch
strategies. Furthermore, SWANet by He et al. (2024) resonated on frequency domain
utilizations, yet due to the disjoint training strategies of the method, the performance under
extreme low light is constrained. Therefore, with the demonstrations of MSFE integration,
combining spatial and frequency domain information is of high potential, where the frequency

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

23

AMGAN

CHAPTER 02: LITERATURE REVIEW

attribute contributes to the enhancement without the introduction of noise, taking the discretewavelet domain as inspiration for FFT (Shang et al., 2024).
2.5.4 Attention mechanisms in LLIE
Attention mechanisms (AMs), inspired by the HVS, play a key role in LLIE by driving focus
toward regions requiring further attention, thereby improving overall performance (Cao et al.,
2024). The accompanying techniques as spatial, channel, and multi-head attention optimize the
enhancement process (YU, LI and HUA, 2023). For instance, the unsupervised EnlightenGAN
by Jiang et al. (2021) utilized self-regularized attention, while Diff-Retinex combined Retinex
and diffusion perspectives in balancing detail and noise. Yet, when performing in solitude, AMs
face challenges regardless of capabilities. Global Attention Modules (GAMs) enhance global
processing, yet the high computational cost affects in complicating the local detail refinement
(Liu, Shao and Hoffmann, 2021). Embedding Non-Local Networks (NLNs) in U-Net structures
improves the long-range dependency focus yet results in processing overhead, thereby
hindering the real-time performance (Cao et al., 2024). Further down the line, methods such as
DEGAN by Jialiang Zhang et al. (2024), despite their effectiveness in noise alleviation, tend
to struggle with overexposure under non-uniform lighting, parallelly requiring an extensive
amount of labeled data. Therefore, with such promising potential, AMs, through further
research on diverse integration as in this research can assist the enhancement process,
contributing to the overall resultant image.
2.5.5 Complementary learning sub-networks (CLSNs)
Providing reinforcements to the main network in the LLIE process, thereby contributing the
global features in enhancing the main network input, which assists further processing by the
Complementary Learning Sub-Networks (CLSNs) (S Yang et al., 2023). Methods like
LightingNet integrate CLSN in combining the global feature extraction of Res2Net with the
fine-grained learning of ViTs (S Yang et al., 2023). Similarly, STAN by (Zhang et al., 2022),
integrates CLSN in enhancing the interactions between structure and texture sub-networks, in
addressing pertaining non-uniform lighting issues. Therefore, the integration of CLSN in LLIE,
as a reinforcement measure, enables strengthening the feature extraction, processing, and
fusion, thereby resonating on a more sophisticated enhancement (S Yang et al., 2023).

2.6.1.2 Qualitative evaluation
Resonating on the most advanced systems ever created, as a prominent IQA, the unique
perception and processing capabilities of the HVS are considered (Tian et al., 2023).
Qualitative evaluation encompasses the comparisons of the visual differences between the
enhanced image and counterpart original low-illumination image, based on HVS perception.
Following (Jize Zhang et al., 2024), other than the (1) standard qualitative evaluation
method, which compared the differences between the two images, subjectively, (2) user
studies that accompany a group (20, ideally) of anonymous/expert personas, evaluating and
choosing the better choice in a sequence of iterative tests, accompanied by other SOTAs, with
a set of guidelines and subjective opinion scores relied on brightness, colorfulness, contrast
factors, and if the enhancement is free from over-/under-exposure and artifacts, choosing the
stand-out, are endowed.
2.6.1.3 Efficiency evaluators
As transformer networks tend to produce quality results, they are limited by the computational
burden that is to be borne alongside the process. Likewise, to evaluate the performance
efficiency, Floating Point Operations (FLOPs) for time complexity and parameter count
(Params) for space complexity of the model are utilized (L Wang et al., 2024).

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

27

AMGAN

CHAPTER 02: LITERATURE REVIEW

2.6.2 Benchmarking of LLIE method
In focus on benchmarking the performance of the proposed method with other SOTAs
(RetinexNet (Wei et al., 2018), KinD (Zhang, Zhang and Guo, 2019), EnlightenGAN (Jiang et
al., 2021), LLFlow (Wang et al., 2021), ZeroDCE (Guo et al., 2020) with public
implementation access) in LLIE, specifically in environments under non-uniform lighting
scenarios. These methods are evaluated on a widely used, diversified range of validation sets
from datasets such as LSRW (L Wang et al., 2024), LOL-v2real (Yang et al., 2021), SICE (Cai,
Gu and Zhang, 2018), LIME (Guo, Li and Ling, 2017), and MIT-Adobe FiveK (Bychkovsky
et al., 2011), including varied scenes, better for generalizability targeted training. The
benchmarking process extends to the crucial by comparatively analyzing the quantitative
metric scores (i.e. PSNR, SSIM, MSE, NIQE, IE as mentioned earlier) and qualitative
assessments for visual coherence inspections of the produced enhancement results of each
method. Additionally, the efficiency of the proposed method is compared with the SOTAs by
evaluating the model complexity by analyzing the spatial complexity and time complexity.

2.7 Chapter summary
This Literature Review meticulously dissected the landscape of LLIE by mapping out the
section as the problem domain, surveying existing methodologies, and reviewing the
technological advancements. Initializing with a conceptual overview, the review critically
evaluates numerous enhancement techniques, thereby underscoring the separate integrations of
multi-scale feature extraction and attention mechanisms within U-Net-based and kindred GAN
frameworks. This comprehensive assessment, not limited to highlighting the gaps in existing
methods, additionally has set the groundwork for the proposed architecture. The posit strategies
for the evaluation of the architecture against the SOTAs are demonstrated in the validation of
the potential to significantly advance the quality of LLIE. This chapter has laid a robust
foundation for further explorations, with a focal point on refining the review techniques in a
collaborative landscape, expanding the possibilities in enhancing practical performance,
especially in edge cases.

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

28

AMGAN

CHAPTER 03: METHODOLOGY

CHAPTER 03: METHODOLOGY
3.1 Chapter overview
The proportionality of the success of any project is directly mapped to the methodologies
accompanied for addressing the diverse aspects of the venture. In prospect, this chapter expands
on focusing on the methodologies selected for the LLIE research, development, and
components of project management in the LLIE research. Additionally, a timeline sketch in
correlation to the deliverables of this project is provided for the conclusion of this chapter.

3.2 Research methodology
The following table provides an overview of the selected scientific methodology based on the
conventional Research ‘Onion’ Model, presented by (Saunders et al., 2019).
Research philosophy

Pragmatism is selected for the research undertaken. LLIE on
non-uniform lighting scenarios is an ill-posed problem with an
indefinite solution relying on qualitative and quantitative
spheres, presenting pragmatism as it supports experimentation
linked with both positivistic and interpretive aspects (mixed
method), for the optimal approach in achieving research goals.

Research approach

Deductive reasoning was chosen due to its alignment with the
theoretical hypothesis and existing research techniques. This
involves extensive experimentation with deep learning
architectures, like, GANs, CLSN, AMs, and MSFEs to align
with the hypothesis and supervise edge cases in enhancement.

Research methodological The mixed method is selected, concatenating quantitative
choice

(experiments,

survey)

and

qualitative

(interviews,

observations) inspections. This approach ensures a thorough
analysis and data retrieval for tasks of LLIE.
Research strategy

The research strategy includes experiments and surveys to
harvest quantitative data during the training phase of DL
models, which require precise tuning. During later stages,
interviews and self-evaluations will retrieve qualitative data,
thereby validating the prototype of the research.

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

AMGAN
Research time horizon

CHAPTER 03: METHODOLOGY

Data collection periods in research are either cross-sectional
(single point in time) or longitudinal (extended period). For
efficient evaluation, a cross-sectional approach is chosen,
involving data retrievals at a single point, suiting the project.

Research data collection Data collection will target domain researchers, industry
and analysis

experts, and computational photography specialists. Aimed
for 200 questionnaire responses for diversely broad data, and
15 interviews for detailed insights. Data analysis will include
both quantitative (mean, median, mode, standard deviation)
and qualitative subject identification to enhance the findings.

3.3 Development methodology
Methodologies encouraging iterative development, flexibility, and continuous advancement
coordinate well with the research goals. Therefore, the prototyping model is chosen for the
aptitude to facilitate ideation, development, experts feedback, and iterative refinement. This
approach enables continuous enhancements based on evolving literature and evaluations
throughout the project tenure.

3.4 Project management methodology
Agile PRINCE2, which amalgamates traditional PRINCE2 and Agile principles, is chosen for
the project management. Resonating on the iterative developments, improvements, and
meeting the desired expectations of the project, Agile PRINCE2 stood out as an optimal and
effective methodology with consideration of the blending of structured control in project
management and flexible adaptability in the under-taken dynamic project, ensuring the focused
deliverance of high-quality outcomes with stakeholder expectation and risk management.
The various methodologies that were identified as candidates in the selection are presented and
discussed in APPENDIX C.4., thereby proving the selection for the current research.

4.1 Chapter overview
This chapter provides a comprehensive analysis of the system requirements of the AMGAN
for handling non-uniform lighting with generalization in LLIE. It extends to identifying and
evaluating the roles and expectations of key stakeholders, visualized through the rich picture
diagram, stakeholder onion model, and context diagram to interpret the interactions and the
environment. The requirements are deliberately elicited as functional and non-functional,
guided by the MoSCoW principle. Additionally, the use case diagrams and descriptions provide
an exhaustive understanding of operations. This chapter establishes the quintessential for
system development, ensuring all stakeholder needs and system goals are met with precision.

4.4 Selection of requirement elicitation methodologies
For this project, multiple requirement elicitation methodologies were recruited to gather
accurate, actionable insights from the stakeholders above. The following table profiles the
chosen methodologies and their purpose in ensuring the system meets stakeholder needs.
Method 1: Literature review
A comprehensive literature review was conducted to identify research gaps, and the reviewal
of existing systems in LLIE, latterly, better focused on utilizing GAN, CLSN, AM, MSFE
techniques. This constructed a supportive background in understanding current limitations,
best practices, and shaping the foundational design of the proposed system.
Method 2: Surveys (questionnaire)
Surveys, specifically questionnaires, were distributed among the end-users (general public,
students) with the intention towards collecting quantitative feedback on expected usability
and system performance preferences. The survey contributed to the process of identifying
user expectations for LLIE and provided inputs for further refining the user-facing features,
thereby improving the complete experience of a LLIE system, which are of immense value.
Method 3: Interviews
Structured interviews with domain experts (i.e. AI experts, Image processing experts) were
conducted to gather in-depth qualitative insights into system requirements and technical

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

37

AMGAN

CHAPTER 04: SOFTWARE REQUIREMENT SPECIFICATION

challenges encountered with the circulation in LLIE task. This method contributed to provide
detailed feedback on specific image processing features and GAN/CLSN (CNN) model
performance, ensuring alignment with industry expected standards.
Method 4: Experiments
Experiments were conducted quantitative performance of the system, particularly the
effectiveness of the cross integration of the GAN, CLSN, AM, and MSFE techniques in
enhancing low-light images. This method enabled the validation of the system performance
against the objective metrics as image quality proportional to the layer complexity.
Method 5: Observations
Real-time observations of the interactions of the system with the end-users were performed
to gather qualitative feedback on the usability and practical behavior aspects of the system.
Observations were crucial for recognizing improvements required in the workflow strategies
and refining the presentation of objectively proven biproducts of the system.
Method 6: Self-evaluations
As a part of the development process in the research, self-evaluations were conducted
throughout the timeline, allowing the implementer (author) to reflect on the functionality,
design and performance of the system progression. The method enables continuous
opportunities for self-critique, leading to improvements in the iterative prototyping phase.
Method 7: Prototyping
Prototyping was utilized in iterative development and testing of the system, thereby enabling
stakeholders to review and in turn provide feedback in early-stage prototypes. This
continuous refinement enabled by prototyping ensures that the model components (GAN and
CLSN) were optimized, and user requirements met through real-world testing.
Table 8: Selected requirement elicitation methodologies.

The excluded requirement elicitation methodologies and reason behind the choice is
discussed in APPENDIX D.1.

4.5 Discussions on findings

groups is analyzed based on information in need and methodologies suited in combination. The
breakdown of these stakeholders is presented in APPENDIX D.2.

The table below unwraps in brief the findings gathered through the literature review.

AMGAN

Finding

Citation

Problem domain
Imprecise non-uniform illumination handling, where the (Zhang et al., 2022, 2024;
adaptation of a globally uniform enhancement strategy is Huang et al., 2024, 2024;
promoted, resulting in over-enhancement and detail and texture L Wang et al., 2024;
feature loss. Models, in general, tend to overexpose images with Shang et al., 2024)
non-uniform lighting, especially with the presence of complex
light sources or noise, thereby leading to a sub-optimal image
enhancement outcome (localized overexposure, inadequate
restoration, and distortion in the image). Herewith, the models
struggle with enhancing under-illuminated areas and is
delimited in suppressing overexposed regions effectively.
Research Domain
Utilizing both the spatial domain and frequency domain feature, (Hai et al., 2023; Han,
extracted to improve the generalization capabilities, while Zhou and Zeng, 2023; He
retaining the deep information in an image for color, detail and et al., 2024; Shang et al.,
texture, and overall image coherence enhancement in producing 2024; Yao et al., 2024)
results. As reflected, multi-scale feature utilization of spatial
and frequency spectral further enhance brightness, suppress
noise and optimize performance with a higher potential in
mixed combination.
As to resonate on the requirement of utilizing attention (Liu et al., 2023; Fu et al.,
mechanisms which distribute weights based on attention needs 2024; X Wang et al.,
in regions of degraded image needs to be taken a step further by 2024; Zhang et al., 2024)
efficiently extending the AM use in complex environments, as
suggested in literature, to improve performance in non-uniform
lighting scenes.
Reliance on the generator network in GANs to produce (Yang et al., 2023)
enhancement results thereby validated by the discriminator does
leave room for improvement as enhancement challenges are
likely to be overlooked, thereby resonating the importance of a
reinforcement branch to the GAN. Here, CLSN act as a
reinforcement branch, producing partial enhancement which is

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

39

AMGAN

CHAPTER 04: SOFTWARE REQUIREMENT SPECIFICATION

quintessential to fill the missing block of the GAN, thereby
contributing to a globally robust feature enhancement driving
specialization in the respective network, without overlooking
LLIE challenges (brightness, color, exposure control).
While GAN-based models significantly improve LLIE, they (L Wang et al., 2024)
have a tendency window for limitations, such as image
distortions, noise and other recurring factors. Therefore, to
address the minute inadequacies, CLSN, MSFE, and AM are
utilized to overcome such challenges overlooked by the SOTAs,
thereby improving the performance.

4.5.2 Interview

4.5.3 Survey
A survey questionnaire (with a combination of close-ended and open-ended questions), was
conducted with the focus of gathering user requirements, thereby identifying key
functionalities for the proposed AMGAN system. This elicitation process enabled assurance
that the system aligns with the needs and expectations of the user to solve limitations and
challenges posed by the existing solutions. The author was able to gather 179 survey responses.
Question

How often do you encounter images that are difficult to see due to low or
uneven lighting?

Aim of question As to intervene the frequency with which users experience challenges
with low and uneven lighting in images, thereby resonating the
importance of an DL-based image enhancement solution.

Findings & conclusion
These findings lead towards the substantial need for a solution that is in fact capable of LLIE,
highlighting that the tool is built with broad practical relevance. Through the addressing of
such a widely experienced issue, the system can effectively cater both casual and
professional users, thereby underscoring the potential impact and presence across various
user groups identified through the responses received.
Question

What types of visual degradations do you commonly notice in low-light
images?

Aim of question To identify the most prevalent range of visual degradations encountered
in low-light images, thus focusing on the key areas requiring
enhancement in the proposed solution.

4.5.5 Experiment
To optimize the performance efficacy of the AMGAN method, numerous experiments were
conducted, focusing on the areas of hyperparameter tuning, image data normalization,
optimizer selection, and data augmentation utilizations of variety and datasets to avoid
overfitting. Since both the representative models, GAN and CLSN, were implemented from
scratch, precise experimentations were required to meet the expected convergence rates and
enhancement. The below table summarizes the experimental findings.

normalization

techniques ranging from min-max normalization to Z-score normalization

methods

were utilized for experimentation. As a result, min-max normalization
circulated to be effective due to the scaling of pixel values within the range
of 0 and 1, allowing better learning.

Optimizer

For the experimental purposes, both the Adam and SGD (Stochastic

selection

Gradient Descent) were evaluated. Yet, the recent and most used

(Adam

SGD)

performance in allowing faster convergence and stable loss minimization
through epochs. As per the reason to discard SGD, it demonstrated slow
convergence, thereby appreciating the efficiency of Adam optimizer.

4.11 Chapter summary
In this chapter, key stockholder identification and their interactions with the LLIE system were
analyzed in detail. A comprehensive evaluation of user requirements of the image enhancement
tool was provided through diagrams like the context diagram and stakeholder onion model.
Requirement elicitation techniques ranging from stakeholder interaction-based surveys and
interviews and other elicitation-like observations and experiments were employed, thereby
gathering the functional and non-functional requirements of the proposed LLIE method, which
are the core for developing the system under research. Use cases were defined in-depth, thereby
reaching the primary user interactions and the extending functionalities, which are aligned with
LLIE. This chapter concludes with a well-structured, prioritized list of requirements organized
according to the MoSCoW principle, aligning with user and enhancement system objectives.

CHAPTER 06: DESIGN

CHAPTER 06: DESIGN
6.1 Chapter overview
This chapter presents the architectural and design aspects of the proposed AMGAN, focused
on high-level and low-level designs, system workflows, and the interactions of the components
in the system. It provides detailed insights into the design choices for achieving the functional
and non-functional requirements of the system. This chapter outlines UI wireframes to
exemplify user interactions and presenting technical outtakes supporting the implementation.

6.2 Design goals
The desired design goals to be achieved by the system are specified in the table below.
ID

Goal

Description

DG01

Performance

The system must efficiently process degraded low-light images with
minimal latency, while preserving the inherent details and visual
coherency. Leverage MSFE and AM towards a high performant system
without compromising image quality.

DG02

Scalability

The design should enable varying image sizes and types, thereby
allowing the system to scale effectively to diverse real-world low-light
conditions. The architecture enables rigid processing and efficient
memory utilization to large domain-specific or non-specific datasets.

DG03

Usability

The system must provide an intuitive user interface, enabling both the
novice and expert level users to easily uploaded images, proceed with
the enhancements, and review produced results.

DG04

Efficiency

The model focus on the computational cost and enhancement quality
balance through optimized resource usage. The design should enable a
trade-off between image processing speed and accuracy of the
enhancement without throttling the system resource usage.

DG05

Modularity

The architecture is modular to allow iterative updates, improvements,
and integrations with existing LLIE techniques. Each module as data
processing, CLSN, GAN, and UI, should be independent and cohesive.

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

57

AMGAN
DG06

CHAPTER 06: DESIGN

Accessibility

The system should include the single-click enhancement, for effortless
system usage to all users, including non-technical personas. Therefore,
accessibility and ease without complex manual intervention is enabled.

DG07

Correctness

The intricate factors as color fidelity, texture and crucial image detail
must be accurately preserved, reaching real-world down-stream CV
requirements relying on a consistent and reliable enhancement result.
Table 19: Design goals.

6.3 System architecture design
The proposed low-light image enhancement system follows a three-tiered architecture, thereby
enabling a structured and efficient processing workflow. This architecture consists of the data,
logic, and presentation tier, each catering a distinct role in facilitating seamless data processing,
model execution, and system-user interaction.
6.3.1 Architectural diagram

Figure 10: Architectural diagram (self-composed).

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

58

AMGAN

CHAPTER 06: DESIGN

6.3.2 Discussion of tiers of the architecture
Data tier
•

Degraded input image storage – Stores the uploaded low-light images before they
undergo processing by the enhancement pipeline. These degraded image data serve as
inputs for enhancements and evaluation phases.

•

Trained image enhancement model storage – Contains the well-trained CLSN and GAN
models, which are then utilized to enhance image factors such as brightness, color
consistency, texture, and detail enhancement, in collaboration. These models are loaded
back into the system once the enhancement is initiated.

•

Enhanced image storage – Temporarily stores the processed image that has undergone the
enhancement pipeline before they are presented to the user for comparison and evaluation.

•

Model logs (performance data) – Stores both performance evaluation metrics (PSNR,
SSIM, MSE, NIQE, IE for both test and train phases) and the produced results of the
enhancements with overall plotting to provide insights into the enhancement quality.

•

Dataset storage – Contains datasets that are combined and utilized to train the
enhancement models, thereby ensuring robust well-trained, and tested models.

Logic tier
•

Input image (degraded) data loader – Loads the degraded image input by the user to the
system in order to undergo enhancement processing.

•

Image input preprocessor – Handles the image preprocessing tasks of resizing the image
to 256x256 resolution, normalization, and other candidate transformations as to prepare the
images to be passed into the input layers of the networks.

•

CLSN model (brightness enhancement module) – Improves illumination component of
the degraded image, through the generation of an inverse grey map as the attention map, to
complement the GAN network with such reinforcements.

•

GAN model (detail enhancement module) – Takes the CLSN-enhanced result and
proceeds to further enhance the image in the aspects of color consistency, detail, and texture
through the utilization of both the spatial and frequency features of the image.

•

Output image (enhancement) data loader – Retrieves and loads the enhancement results
from storage to be displayed in the user interface, thereby enabling side-by-side comparison
and evaluation.

•

Train enhancement model – Handles the training and retraining phases of the CLSN and
GAN model components of the entire solution. It includes:

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

59

AMGAN

CHAPTER 06: DESIGN

o Model training module – Executes the training process of accompanied networks.
o Dataset loader – Loads training datasets from the data tier to support the training
phases in model optimizations.
•

Backend proxy (API) – Serves as the communication layer between the presentation and
logic tier of the three-tier architecture, thereby handling user requests, and proceeding
towards passing them to the appropriate processing components.

Presentation tier
•

User input interface (landing page) – Allows the user to upload low-light images that are
experiencing degradation, and to select the enhancement method (CLSN only or full
enhancement utilizing both CLSN and GAN).

•

Model selection module – Enables the user to choose between the available enhancement
options of a single model (CLSN) or complete enhancement (GAN accompanied by the
CLSN for a full enhancement), before further processing is followed.

•

Processing screen – Presents the real-time progress updates to the user, while the
enhancement phases have started, as to keep the user in the loop.

•

Output image display – Provides a side-by-side comparison of the original degraded
image, which was input by the user to the system to undergo enhancement processing, and
the enhancement results from the final GAN network, allowing the user to visually compare
and evaluate the improvements by the system. Additionally, to download the enhancements.

•

Model performance metric data – Presents the calculated enhancement metrics, as to
evaluate the effectiveness of the enhancement process. The metrics span from quantitative
metrics such as PSNR, to enhancement time, speed, etc.

•

Model train configuration (CLI) – Session based on CLI for configuring and retraining
the enhancement networks on improved datasets, updated parameters and weights.

The AMGAN system accompanies the Object-Oriented Analysis and Design (OOAD)
methodology, as discussed in methodology chapter. This methodology is selected for the
underlining of modularity, reusability, and abstraction, which thereby aligns with the
requirements of the AMGAN system.
