6.5 Algorithm design
The AMGAN system consists of inverse grey map and spatial domain and frequency domain
feature extraction, to enhanced low-light images. This approach consists of two primary steps,
Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

61

AMGAN

CHAPTER 06: DESIGN

1. Complementary Learning Sub-Network (CLSN), which is inspired by the usage of a
reinforcement branch by the LightingNet method (Yang et al., 2023), thereby acting on
generating an inverse gray map using the illumination constraints (Fan et al., 2022), which
is utilized as the attention map to enhance the brightness component, adaptively.
2. GAN-based image refinement, a U-Net-based generator, extracts the intricate details of
an image, which is of higher importance for coherency of image features, by utilizing both
the spatial domain and frequency domain features of the degraded image. A dual-Markov
discriminator is accompanied to make the most use of the extracted features.

Figure 13: Pseudocode – algorithm (self-composed).

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

62

AMGAN

CHAPTER 06: DESIGN

Figure 14: High-level architecture of the AMGAN method (self-composed).

6.5.1 Complementary Learning Sub-Network (CLSN)
Illumination constraint-based inverse gray map
The CLSN model takes over the role of generating an inverse gray map based on the
illumination constraint equation inspired by the method MLLEN-IC (Fan et al., 2022). This
process allows the model to drive attention towards the dark regions, which intentionally
require more attention than the partially illuminated image; thereby, the attention map applied
to the original low-light image selectively enhances dark regions, resolving over brightening.
The inverse gray map as the attention map
The illumination constraint Φ(i,j) is considered in aspects of all three color channels in RGB
(R- red, G- green, B-blue) as inspired by Fan et al. (2022),
Φ(i,j) = ϕR(i,j) ⊗ ϕG(i,j) ⊗ ϕB(i,j)
Where, ϕR(i,j), ϕG(i,j), and ϕB(i,j) are the illumination constraints for the red, green, and blue
channels, respectively, rather than generating the illumination constraint for the degraded
image as one single channel, which leads to loss of intricate channel-specific details of the
image (Fan et al., 2022). Here the ⊗ operation denotes the element-wise multiplication.
Here, each illumination constraint of a channel (R, G, B) can be denoted as,

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

63

AMGAN

CHAPTER 06: DESIGN

Where src(i,j) are the pixel intensities at coordinates at position (i,j). And max and min are the
respective minimum and maximum intensity values in the channel under consideration. And τ
and ρ represent the minimum and maximum values within the specific channel under
consideration. The produced result of this is an inverse grey map, which is then multiplied by
the original degraded image, thereby selectively providing strength to enhance the brightness
of the regions of the image. The CLSN model implementation incorporates a U-Net-like
encoder-decoder architectural implication, which includes skip connections, ensuring both
global and local image context, leading the intricate detail preservation.
6.5.2 GAN-based image refinement process
As with the partial-enhancement produced by the CLSN step, it is passed forward to the input
layer of the GAN model, which extends the enhancement by extracting not only spatial features
but also the frequency domain features using a technique called Fast Fourier Transform (FFT),
thereby guiding the overall image color profiles and brightness, and extend to maintaining the
intricate details and texture of the image, as to maintain the structure of the degraded image.
Fast Fourier Transform (FFT) for frequency domain processing
Targeting the detail and texture through the utilization of high-frequency details, the GAN
accompanies Fourier features into the usual spatial domain practices. Here the 2D Discrete
Fourier Transform (DFT), which is utilized in the system, can be resorted as Shang et al. (2024),

Where f(x,y) is the spatial domain image, which contributes to enhancing the color profile,
contrast, and further brightness enhancements of the image. The leftover detail and texture
factors of the image, which are left out in the majority of the enhancement methods, are taken
over by the frequency domain feature representation, F(u,v), as in the equation. The dimensions
of the image are depicted in the equation as M and N. As the equation describes, in
e−j2π((ux/M)+(vy/N)) is the complex exponential basis function. And then the frequency
domain representation is reconstructed back to the enhanced image through Inverse Fourier
Transform (IFT), as depicted in the equation given (Shang et al., 2024),

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

64

AMGAN

CHAPTER 06: DESIGN

6.5.3 Loss functions in the AMGAN method
As GANs show a tendency towards generating visually interpretable results, in a well-defined
architecture, loss functions contribution for quality is appreciated by the adversarial process.
1. GAN adversarial loss
To fool the discriminator with the generated pseudo image, the generator loss is utilized,
LGAN(G) = Ez∼pz [log(1 − D(G(z)))]
Where D(z) is the image generated by the generator network, and D(G(z)) is the probability
that the generated image is real, determined by the discriminator network.
Likewise, the discriminator utilizes the discriminator loss to maximize it by improving the
classification as real or fake for the images.
LGAN(D) = Ex∼pdata [logD(x)] + Ez∼pz [log(1 − D(G(z)))]
If D(z) is close to 1 and D(G(z)) is close to 0, then the discriminator performance is reliable.
2. Perceptual loss
Determination of the perceptual similarity between the enhancement and the well-lit images is
of immense importance. Therefore, the VGG16-based perceptual loss is utilized in the image
generation components.

LVGG
Where, ϕi(x) are the feature maps accompanied by the i-th VGG16 layer, and Ni is the number
of elements in that specific layer, which thereby assesses the perceptual similarity to determine
the loss values for the enhancement carried out.

and extracting features from the frequency domain in the GAN architecture, while the CLSN
accompanies a three-channel-based attention map. So, expanding on that note, this section
details the implementation of the core functionalities, starting with dataset handling, CLSNbased attention map generation, GAN-based enhancement, and calculating the evaluation
metrics, optimization strategies, and training strategies accompanied for the system.

need. Images are,

7.3.2 CLSN reinforcement network implementation
The CLSN model follows an encoder-decoder CNN architectural structure, which generates an
inverse gray map for each color channel (RGB color space) for attention-driven enhancement.
•

__init__, defined the convolutional layers, batch normalization, and skip connections for
the image feature extraction.

Forward propagation processes the input image through the encoding and decoding

7.3.3 GAN-based enhancement implementation
The GAN model consists of a U-Net-based generator and a dual Markov discriminator for
enhancing the CLSN-refined images. The implementation is structured into:
Generator initialization (__init__), which defined the U-Net layers, frequency feature
extraction using FFT, and skip connections.

Frequency feature integration (forward) applied FFT to extract high-frequency
components and then utilize that information to integrate them with the spatial features.

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

73

AMGAN

CHAPTER 07: IMPLEMENTATION

Discriminator (__init__ and forward pass), implements the patch-based discriminator for
adversarial training for the entire image as a whole and through patches of image.

Peak Signal-to-Noise Ratio (PSNR), which measures the quality of the enhanced image

Structural Similarity Index Measure (SSIM), which measures the consistency in terms of
the structural coherency between the enhanced image and the ground truth. Higher, the better.

8.3.3 Results and benchmarking
The proposed method was benchmarked against the SOTA LLIE methods, and the comparison
were based on the key aspects. Such as,
•

Quantitative metric evaluation, with PSNR, and SSIM scores.

•

Qualitative assessment, for visual comparison of the enhancements, through HVS.

As for the benchmarking a determined set of parameter configurations were used for each
dataset utilizations. And as for the LSRW dataset, the following parameters were tuned in, as,
•

Learning rate: 5x10-4 = 0.0005 (for the generator) and 1x10-3 = 0.001 (for the discriminator)

•

Number of epochs: 600 epochs

•

Learning rate scheduler: Cosine Annealing LR from 5x10-4 to 5x10-5 over the 600 epochs.

•

With Adam Optimizer with 0.0 weight decay.

8.7 Edge case testing
8.7.1 Extreme low-light conditions
The model was tested with images with the presence of extremely low illumination levels.

Figure 20: Extreme low-light conditions - comparative results (self-composed).

8.7.2 Extreme low-light conditions with non-uniform illumination.
In addition to the extremely low-illumination levels, testing was extended to scenarios that also
included non-uniformity in illumination distribution wherever it was presented.

Figure 21: Extreme low-light conditions with non-uniform illumination - comparative results
(self-composed).

Observation from testing upon extreme low-light conditions and with the existence of nonuniformity in lighting:

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

86

AMGAN
•

CHAPTER 08: TESTING

The CLSN was able to effectively drive enhancement in adjusted levels by identifying the
darker regions in existence, thereby providing assurance that the brightness factor was
enhanced by focusing on the under-exposed areas more while avoiding over-exposure in
well-illuminated regions.

•

The GAN proceeded with the detail and texture enhancement in particular, while it found
that extremely dark environments create a tendency toward the generation of artifacts, as
can be expected, at such a degree of degradation.

8.7.3 Compression artifact testing
As with the observation of the behavior of the system in processing an input image that had
undergone compression, a low-quality image was introduced as an input.

Figure 22: Compression artifact testing - comparative results (self-composed).

Observations from the input of low-quality conditions include that,
•

The CLSN was able to preserve the brightness factor across the image, while mitigating
the under-exposed scenes, in presence.

•

The GAN was able to enhance the detail and texture information within the image while
allowing compression artifacts due to the involvement of the frequency aspect of the model.

•

To mitigate, the Fourier domain feature extraction was gated to adjust the involvement
factor while still contributing to emphasize the texture and detail features of the image,
which are intricate and are of high importance for the image in enhancement.

primarily stemmed from hardware resources, dataset constraints, and un-tested real-world and
domain-specific scenarios. Such identified limitations are.

8.9 Testing results and discussion
The testing phase demonstrated the level of effectiveness in enhancing low-light images by the
proposed method in both quantitative and qualitative aspects of evaluation. The AMGAN
Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

88

AMGAN

CHAPTER 08: TESTING

prototype achieved a PSNR of 18+ dBs and SSIM of 0.439 under the LSRW dataset and with
the same competitive landscape in the datasets selected, which can be considered a step forward
from the PoC level, which denotes a significant take on the image coherency in both visual and
structural aspects. Qualitative evaluations also demonstrated that the enhanced image was
closely resembling with the ground truth image, which again denotes the structural integrity
and preservation of details within the image tensor. However, further refinements in uplifting
the naturalness and the vivid color profiles are possible to show a much closer resemblance to
the ground truth. Despite this self-evaluation, the current implementation already showcases
notable improvements to the standard baseline, act as the CLSN only method.

8.10 Testing phase miscellaneous
As the models were produced as a result of rigorous testing and evaluations, the progress
(training time, and checkpointing) screenshots have been attached in the APPENDIX G.2.

8.11 Chapter summary
This chapter presented testing methodologies utilized to validate the functionality,
performance, and robustness of the proposed AMGAN method. Various testing strategies, such
as functional, non-functional, and edge case testing, were conducted for the reliability
assessment. As a key outtake, the model demonstrated better overall image coherency with
higher PSNR (18.2278 dB) and SSIM (0.4594) scores in LSRW and, also, compeititve scores
in other selected datasets, showcasing the effectivity of the LLIE method while maintaining
the intricate details of the image. Benchmark comparison depicted a competitive landscape
uplifted with only minor refinements needed for color and naturalness as in improvement.

CHAPTER 09: EVALUATION

CHAPTER 09: EVALUATION
9.1 Chapter overview
Upon implementation, a comprehensive evaluation is quintessential for validating the
completion of the gathered requirements in Chapter 4, by the proposed LLIE method. This
chapter details the self-evaluations of author and feedback from domain and technical experts.

9.2 Evaluation methodology and approach
As the primary focus of this research, design, and implementation of the AMGAN method for
LLIE, both qualitative and quantitative evaluations are essential to validate the effectiveness
of the method. A qualitative analysis was conducted through the gathering of feedback from
domain and technical experts to assess the conceptual soundness, technical complexity, and
real-world applicability of the proposed LLIE method. In parallel, a quantitative evaluation
was carried out to measure the quality of the enhancement, across multiple datasets. This
chapter will present the thematic analysis of the qualitative feedback obtained from the
aforementioned. Furthermore, user-studies were conducted to evaluate the generalization.

9.3 Evaluation criteria
Before proceeding, well-defined criteria are an integral step to ensure that all aspects of the
research are systematically assessed. The table in APPENDIX H.1 outlines the evaluation
criteria used in this study based on the LLIE (CV) domain and technical expert feedback.

9.4 Self-evaluation
Theme

Evaluation by the author

Concept of The concept of Attention-Driven Multi-Scale GAN with the reinforcement of
the

a Complementary Learning Sub-Network (CLSN) for LLIE is novel in the

research

domain of deep learning-based image processing. Unlike the traditional
enhancement techniques that rely purely on the brightness and contrast factors
and their respective adjustments, the proposed method leverages a fusion of
spatial domain and frequency domain feature processing, thereby retaining the
intricate image details, while also adaptively enhancing the brightness factor
to tackle non-uniformity of light distribution. The introduction of the CLSN as
to produce the inverse gray map with weights of attention distribution further

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

AMGAN

CHAPTER 09: EVALUATION

strengthens the method, providing a uniquely effective and efficient
mechanism to selectively enhance the underexposed areas. This project
successfully advances the GAN-based LLIE, proceeding to a contributory step
towards improved real-world applicability in down-stream vision tasks such
as

computational photography, autonomous

systems, and semantic

segmentation.
Scope and The field of LLIE has been widely explored, yet most of the advanced methods
depth of the are developed by research labs and industry leaders with extensive resources.
project

This project, despite being conducted at an undergraduate level was able to
enable effective integration and optimization of SOTA deep learning
architectures such as GANs, Fourier-based feature extraction, and attention
mechanisms (more specifically inverse grey maps as an efficient alternative to
the well know multi-head self-attention used in ViTs). The scope of the
research was carefully refined to ensure feasibility while maintaining the
technical depth of the research. Furthermore, the study covers a
comprehensive workflow, including dataset utilizations, model training,
hyperparameter tuning, and extensive evaluation using PSNR, SSIM, NIQE,
and IE metrics. Given the complexity of the project, it exceeds typical
undergraduate research expectations, thereby pushing the boundaries of what
can be achieved within the constrained academic tenure.

System

and

multi-scale

feature

extraction.

Model

The core model implementation was executed successfully by following

implement-

structured deep learning methodologies and rigorous testing protocols. The

tation

system, developed in PyTorch, utilized the optimized CUDA enabled GPU
accelerations, optimized data utilization and handling pipelines, and structured
logging of training process. The adversarial training process was stabilized
using progressive learning techniques, ensuring a smooth GAN convergence,
which is a challenging task in adversarial training. Finally, the model
evaluation yielded high-quality, balanced and complete enhancement results,
thereby confirming the effectiveness of the enhancement process, while
preserving the intricate details (through FFT utilizations). Moving further on,
increased optimization scales for a more computationally efficient model
would enable suitability.

interface was developed with increased usability and accessibility. The
prototype validates the practical applicability of the research, with a
demonstration of a strong potential for down-stream vision tasks on distinct
environments.

9.8 Limitations of evaluation
The evaluation process encountered challenges primarily due to the limited experts in the LLIE
domain and the GAN networks. Additionally, the resource constraints led to the difficulty in
conducting extensive large-scale testing across more real-world datasets than the already
included SOTA datasets. While the collected feedback was comprehensive and valuable,
broader insights could have been obtained with access to additional computational resources.
Despite these limitations, the evaluation provided impactful, meaningful, and well-structured
feedback, thereby ensuring the thorough assessment of the LLIE domain research.
The complete breakdown of the functional and non-functional requirements is discussed in
APPENDIX H.7.

9.9 Chapter summary
This chapter presented a structured evaluation of the AMGAN method for non-uniform LLIE.
The evaluation methodology included self-assessment, expert reviews, and thematic analysis
across key criteria established beforehand, such as concept novelty, project complexity, system
architecture, quality of implementation, the performance of the model, usability, and expert
feedback. The evaluators acknowledged the innovative hybrid LLIE approach, where the
system was praised in multiple factors. Finally, the evaluation of functional and non-functional
requirements with the achievements of the design goals was discussed and presented.

CHAPTER 10: CONCLUSION

CHAPTER 10: CONCLUSION
10.1 Chapter overview
This chapter presents the final reflection on the research journey of developing the AMGAN
method for LLIE. It highlights the achievements of the aims and objectives of the project, the
application of course knowledge, the use of both existing and newly acquired technical skills,
and the fulfillment of learning outcomes. It also discusses the challenges encountered and how
they were tackled, the deviations from the initial plan, limitations identified through testing,
and the potential future enhancements. The chapter concludes by summarizing the contribution
to the body of knowledge and offering the final remarks on the proposed AMGAN research.

10.2 Achievements of research aims and objectives
10.2.1 Achievement of the research aim
This research project aims to design, develop, and evaluate a generalized (i.e. with inclusivity
of non-uniform light scenarios), and robust low-light image enhancement Generative
Adversarial Network architecture with a complementary learning sub-network utilizing
attention mechanism and multi-stage feature extraction.
This aim was successfully achieved by designing and developing the proposed
AMGAN architecture, which combined both the spatial and frequency domain learning
through a U-Net-based GAN reinforced by a CLSN that enhances non-uniform low-light image
regions using inverse grey maps. The system was rigorously evaluated using quantitative and
qualitative measures across standard datasets, demonstrating competitive performance. The
final prototype showed significant improvement in handling diverse lighting scenarios,
validating the generalization and robustness of the model.
10.2.2 Achievement of objectives
All objectives stated in Chapter 01 were successfully met. The status of each objective is
denoted and discussed in APPENDIX I.1.

10.3 Utilization of knowledge from the course
The proposed AMGAN research was impacted by the requirement of a vast pool of knowledge,
which the author was fortunate to have gained a strong foundation through exposure to a range
of modules completed during the academic tenure. Among them, a few that stood out are,

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

95

AMGAN
•

Mathematics for computing

•

Object-oriented programming

•

Algorithms: theory, design and implementation

•

Software development group project.

CHAPTER 10: CONCLUSION

For detailed justifications, see the APPENDIX I.2.

10.4 Use of existing skills
Full-stack web development – The author has gained experience in full-stack development
through the experience gained as an intern at IFS, and with the skills developed through web
development modules at the institution.
Machine learning/ deep learning – Concepts learned through the coursework assessments
from the modules such as machine learning and software development group projects were
critical in understanding, designing, and implementing the baseline structure of these models.
Mathematics for computing – Mathematical concepts learned throughout the academic tenure
impacted the transfer of knowledge to techniques such as Fourier transform, frequency domain
analysis, and in utilizing of model optimization techniques and loss functions.

10.5 Use of new skills
•

GAN training and stabilization – Extensive self-learning was required to understand the
GAN-specific challenges, such as mode collapse and adversarial loss balancing, which
cause block artifacts, and to mitigate. This included extensive experimentation with loss
functions, hyperparameters, and training strategies to improve the model convergence.

•

Attention-mechanism integration and Fourier transformation – Acquired advanced
knowledge on applying the inverse gray maps and Fourier-based feature extraction, as a
hybrid approach, based on the foundational knowledge gained from Massive Open Online
Courses (MOOC), including Udemy (specifically from authors such as Mike X Cohen).

•

Neural network block combination – The author had to grasp knowledge and
understanding of how the neural network and block setup impact the convergence and
achievement of the hypothesis. They had to invoke rigorous practice to solidify decisions.

•

ML model deployment – Initially setting up the notebook environment is a challenging
task, as it involves required libraries setup with the resource allocations. The author had to
explore techniques to proceed and host the models in the cloud to avoid local execution.

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

96

AMGAN

CHAPTER 10: CONCLUSION

The achievement of the learning outcomes is unwrapped in APPENDIX I.3.

10.7 Problems and challenges faced
As this is a research project, challenges are unavoidable and are to be tackled. The following
table describes the challenges encountered and the strategies followed to resolve this project.
Problem/ challenge

Mitigation

Table 37: Problems and challenges faced during the project tenure and the mitigations followed.

10.8 Deviations
The author was able to proceed with the planned measures of the project and was able to
successfully achieve the requirements with no identifiable deviations. However, due to the
Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

97

AMGAN

CHAPTER 10: CONCLUSION

technical and resource constraints, expert feedback was received to try and train the CLSN and
GAN in an end-to-end nature once the split training was followed, as it is another way of
approaching the training phase and to accommodate the computation limitations on cloudbased GPU environments. Yet the integration logic was still in line with the initial plan, and
the combined inference pipeline was successfully executed. Additionally, the author was able
to extend the implementation to the ‘desirables’, even with the time constraints.

10.9 Limitations of the research
While the implemented system successfully met all the requirements and strong performance,
certain limitations were observed based on test outputs and unavoidable practical constraints.
•

Narrow application domain – The model performed exceptionally well in majority of the
environments, spanning from moderately to extremely dark environments. Yet extremely
dark LLIE requires specialized adaptations and is a different area of research.

•

Computational constraints – Due to resource limitations, the model was trained using
Tesla T4 GPUs on Google Colab, which inherently required the lowering of resolution (i.e.,
256x256) and balanced data volumes that could be processed. Yet the author reached the
pinnacle of possibilities by using more than 7,500 data samples for model training with
such restriction. This can impact the generalization across very high-resolution datasets.

•

Data diversity – Although the standard datasets were used, combining up to more than
7500 data samples, the model could be tested more across real-world environments such as
nighttime urban (covered yet more explorable), foggy conditions, or motion blue scenarios.

10.10 Future enhancements
Research domain enhancements
•

Joint training of CLSN and GAN – Currently, the two models are trained separately on
feasibility, yet an end-to-end pipeline could improve the coherence and reduce redundancy.

•

Data complexity – Due to the resource constraint, the model was trained on 256x256
resolutions but can be introduced to higher resolutions such as HD, FHD, 4K, and 8K.

•

Fine-tuned learnable attention – Adding a learnable filter for the attention mechanism
that adapts during the training could benefit the diverse scenes and the overall result.

•

Domain-specific enhancement – Training on fixated domain-specific data for applications
such as satellite imagery and underground, where detail preservation is quintessential.

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

98

AMGAN

CHAPTER 10: CONCLUSION

Problem domain enhancements
•

Deployment on edge devices – Model compression and quantization can be researched as
a contribution to the system viability for a more friendly real-time edge device deployment.

•

Advanced user input options – Adding batch uploading capabilities and filter-based
enhancements can make the tool introduce a twist of flexibility for end-users.

10.11 Achievement of the contribution to the body of knowledge
10.11.1 Research domain contributions
•

Proposed a novel hybrid architecture that is not limited to the spatial domain but also
integrates the frequency domain feature learning for a structurally strong enhancement.

•

Introduced the CLSN reinforcement branch to the GAN, with inverse grey attention maps
for adaptive light enhancement, thereby expanding methodological scope in efficient LLIE.

•

Demonstrated a generalized enhancement approach adaptable to different lighting
scenarios and tackling detail and texture loss, contributing to computational photography.

10.11.2 Problem domain contributions
•

Addressed a real-world challenge in LLIE, particularly relevant to the downstream vision
task fields that rely on quality enhancement for accurate decision-making.

•

Validated the proposed method on complex lighting scenes for the persisting issue of
handling non-uniformity in the light distribution using benchmark datasets.

Furthermore, technical/ additional contributions can be found in APPENDIX I.4.

10.12 Concluding remarks
This concludes the journey of researching, designing, and developing a multi-scale GAN
method enhanced by a CLSN for a generalized LLIE. The project tackled a long-existing
problem of non-uniform lighting through the proposal of a novel hybrid architecture that
integrated both the spatial and frequency domain feature information with adaptive attention.
Despite the limited computational resources, the project successfully delivered a technically
robust and innovative solution, well-supported by qualitative and quantitative evaluations. The
project opens avenues for further academic expansions, optimizations, and practical
deployment in evolving fields of computational photography and AI-powered vision systems.

APPENDIX C

APPENDIX C
C.1 Project scope
a. In-scope
In-scope defines the deliverables, focus, and aspects that are within the inclusion of the project.
•

Development of a GAN-based network with a CLSN for LLIE in edge lighting scenarios.

•

Integration of AMs to define the illumination in the LLIE process.

•

Extraction of features from both spatial and channel domains with the MSFE mechanism.

b. Out-scope
Specification of the aspects and constituents that will not be addressed in the project undertaken
will be demonstrated in setting clear boundaries and avoiding scope creep.
•

Development of specialized hardware (inclusive of sensors) for capturing low-light images.

•

Performance analysis on environments of industrial influence (underground mine low-light
image enhancement, etc.) which require further specialization rather than generalization.

APPENDIX C

C.4 Analysis of methodologies
C.4.1 Development methodologies
Methodology

Description

Waterfall model

This rigid and linear development strategy
requires the necessary requirements upfront,
thereby it does not adopt dynamically to the
iterative feedback received from different
stakeholders, limiting the flexibility to cater
timely evolving needs.

Agile Model

This methodology is very flexible, with
incremental development cycles. Inevitably
this approach requires close collaboration
where it makes the development more
complex in solo-driven projects or the
projects that lack continuous inputs from
stakeholders.

RAD (Rapid Application Development)

This approach is very resource intensive as
the development and iteration is quick, as the
name suggests. And does also require user
involvement at the development stage.

Prototyping model

This model enables iterative feedback and
incremental runs in the development, thereby
proving the most ideal for refining the
features based on the stakeholder feedback
and

reflecting

them

through

project

progression.
Conclusion
As the importance of accommodating iterative improvement and further targeted refinement
based on user feedback is key in a research project, and with the flexibility required, the
prototyping model was selected, given the evolving nature of this research.
Table 39: Evaluation of development methodologies.

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

XII

AMGAN

APPENDIX C

C.4.2 Design methodology
Methodology

Description

Waterfall design

A linear approach, which requires complete
implementation in the respective design
phase, which is delimiting flexibility for
refinements along the long run, considering
this project.

Modular design

This design methodology divides the system
into separate distinct modules, yet the result
will be within an isolated environment with
limited integration and feedback.

Agile design

Involves considerable rapid yet flexible
iterations, but would require continuous
collaboration, and is identified unnecessarily
complex for a solo project as such carried out
by the author of this project.

Iterative design

This methodology resonated the cyclic
iterative design, where the adjustments are
based on testing and feedback, which thereby
enables the refinement along the progression
of the project.

Solution
For enabling the involvement in a continuous feedback loop and accompanying adaptive
changes, the iterative design was selected. It ensures design improvements incrementally
based on real-world testing strategy incorporation.
Table 40: Evaluation of design methodologies.

C.4.3 Programming paradigm
Paradigm

Description

Object-oriented programming (OOP)

This paradigm resonates on organizing the
code around the class instances and their
interactions, amalgamating the concepts like
encapsulation,

inheritance,

and

polymorphism. This allows modularization

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

XIII

AMGAN

APPENDIX C

and accompanying reusable components, in
building the project.
Structured programming

This paradigm emphasizes the execution of
sequential and clear control structures (loops,
conditional blocks, etc.), thereby improving
interpretability and reducing complexity, and
would be ideal for a task that takes stepwise
execution and does not require the concepts
defined like inheritance as in OOP paradigm.

Functional programming

Here, the focus is towards functions,
immutability. And is suitable to be utilized in
applications requiring functions that are clear
and testable, with least intertwining.

Procedural programming

This programming paradigm follows a topdown execution, where the program is
accompanied by procedure and routines,
which is simply suitable for straightforward
tasks, which are also simple in nature.

Conclusion
For this project, the object-oriented programming (OOP) was selected considering the fact
that it allows modular design principles incorporation, encapsulation of the components in
the research as GANs and CLSNs, thereby substantially increasing code manageability and
reusability across the board.
Table 41: Evaluation of programming paradigms.

D.3.2 Interview summary
Question

How effective do you think a system designed to enhance low-light images,
particularly in non-uniform lighting conditions, would be on a scale of 1-5?

Responses
P1

“I would say it’s around 4… existing ways are definitely not doing that much
of a good job.”

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

XVIII

AMGAN
P2

APPENDIX D

“I think having this kind of a model would be beneficial… I think maybe 4, it
could be really important in terms of insights.”

P3

“On a scale of 1 to 5, I would say 3.5 because it differs accordingly, but it will
usually improve given the context.”

P4

“I can scale it up to five because they (existing work) are not performing up to
real expectations.”

P5

“From my experience… high-end camera or editing software has a certain limit
to enhancing these kinds of images… I think it is actually a real gap… I’ll go
with 5 out 5.”

Question

What are your thoughts on integrating both GAN and CLSN models for
improving image quality in low-light conditions?

Responses
P1

“GANs itself are definitely applicable for a task like this.”

P2

“Using well-established networks like GANs and CNNs rather than focusing
on large networks and using simple networks where the theory is well
established is beneficial.”

P3

“If the CLSN model has enough data points and can help you improve the
image quality, then obviously, I think integrating that with the generator of the
GAN model is going to improve the quality of the low-light conditions.”

P4

“It makes sense. If you can integrate it, I think it would be great.”

P5

“From what you explained, I feel like... by integrating both together will get
the best of both worlds … and probably end up with better performance and
results. I think it is good that you are going to integrate these things together
rather than going with only one of these models.”

Question

In your opinion, what technical aspects (i.e. color accuracy texture
preservation, or noise reduction) should be prioritized when developing the
low-light image enhancement system?

Responses
P1

“I would put noise reduction as much.”

P2

“I think texture preservation… if we don’t consider preservation, we might
convey invalid information from the image.”

P3

“Texture preservation and noise reduction are two things that you probably
have to focus on… color accuracy is subject…too much focus on color

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

XIX

AMGAN

APPENDIX D

accuracy might end up giving a false representation of what exactly is
captured.”
P4

“Noise reduction should be prioritized because noise is one of the biggest
issues.”

P5

“In night mode…most of the time, it is not perfectly clear, so noise is an issue…
Also, the colors, sometimes is exaggerated… it should be in a level where it
feels natural.”

Question

Can you recommend any specific GAN architectures or optimization
techniques that would be most effective for enhancing images in low-light
conditions?

Responses
P1

“I think you can inform the model with different types of information
separately… maybe like having more channels to the input.”

P2

“I think CycleGAN is one that is used already and because GANs are famous
for super resolution and fixing blurry images.”

P3

“Start with something very simple… try a basic one, if it works, it works, if it
doesn’t go for the next option.”

P4

“Most of the time, noise reduction filters are actually blurring the image. If you
can optimize the blurriness and the noisiness, you can tackle the noise”

P5

“Try different way, compare different approaches, and try to get the best of each
approach.”

Question

What challenges do you anticipate in handling non-uniform lighting conditions
using DL-based systems?

Responses
P1

“The main challenge is about having the correct data.”

P2

“The main problem are the data itself… GANs tend to be unstable to train and
the model might get confused with non-uniform lighting conditions.”

P3

“Preserving authenticity while using the deep learning model to improve the
image quality is like building muscle and losing fat at the same time, which is
not that easy to do.”

P4

“Image quality changes from device to device, and you need to a lot of data.”

P5

“You have to define the solution scope, specify the conditions that your solution
caters to, otherwise it may be challenging to get proper results.”

D.4 Survey analysis
Question

How much of expertise and familiarity do you have with image
editing and enhancement techniques?

Aim of question

To assess the familiarity of the survey participant with image editing,
and related sub-fields thereby guiding elicitation for range of
expertise.

Observation

The depiction resonates that most participants reported basic or intermediate familiarity with
image editing, while a smaller proportion had advanced skills and with no experience.
Findings & conclusion
This ranges suggests the solution should lean towards providing both user-friendly
automated features as the research converges, to cater to novices, and satisfy more skilled
users, ensuring meeting requirement with broader usability across expertise levels.
Question

Have you previously used any software or tools to enhance lowlight images?

Aim of question

To resonate on the prior experience of the participants with
LLIE tools, which will contribute to assessing familiarity with
current solutions and understanding any untouched needs of the
user.

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

XXIII

AMGAN

APPENDIX D

Observation

The results depict a diverse engagement level with image enhancement tools among the
participants. While majority of respondents occasionally utilized such tools, and least of
them use them frequently, and closer to majority have never used such a tool, depicting their
trust with the existing tools. As mentioned, few participants tried these existing tools, but
found them ineffective for their requirements, thereby broadening the gap between the trust
users have on such tools.
Findings & conclusion
These insights emphasize the importance for a reliable enhancement solution that meeting
the user expectations, effectively.
Question

Which of the following tools have you used for low-light image
enhancement?

Aim of question

To understand the usage distribution and preferences of users
for various existing image enhancement tools, particularly those
that have the potential to contribute to the alleviation of lowlight scenarios, effectively. This provides insight into the tools
users are more familiar with and the potential functionality gaps
that can be addresses through research.

Observation

The results depict that Adobe Lightroom and Photoshop are the denoted as the most popular
tools for LLIE, with Snapseed and AI-based tools like Luminar AI following closely. As the

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

XXIV

AMGAN

APPENDIX D

demonstrated preferences for such established tools indicates a user familiarity with manual
adjustments, while the use of AI-driven tools has room for openness to automated solutions.
Findings & conclusion
This trend supports the goals of this research, where developing a specialized DL-based
LLIE tool, filling the identified performance gaps in the current distribution of solutions.
Question

How do you find the process of manually enhancing low-light
images?

Aim of question

To understand user perceptions of the difficulty and required
time investments for manual low-light image enhancement,
thereby gathering statistics on the potential demand for a more
effectively efficient and automated enhancement solution.

Observation

A significant proportion of respondents find the process of enhancing low-light images
manually somewhat time-consuming but manageable, while lesser number of the
respondents describe it as very time-consuming and difficult. Only a least number of
participants find it to be not difficult at all or have never manually enhanced images.
Findings & conclusion
In reflecting on the findings gathered, it highlights a clear-cut opportunity for a streamlined,
DL-based solution that is targeted towards reducing the manual intervention of the user,
while making the enhancement process more efficient and effective, which aligns well with
the objectives of the proposed research.

D.7 Prototyping findings
Prototyping

Findings

phase
Producing inverse Initially, the use of a direct inverse map (1 - grey map pixel values) to
grey

map

with produce the attention map was proved to be less effective in driving

CLSN

attention to the areas which require further enhancement. By being

implementation

influenced by the technique of illumination constraints for all three
channels (R-red, G-green, B-blue), a more nuanced inverse grey map
was possible, as (Fan et al., 2022). This enhanced the accuracy of
determining the underexposed regions which require further attention
in the enhancement process. The scaling of image resolution and the use
of augmentation techniques, such as vertical and horizontal flips, to
diversify the dataset, introduced additional computational complexity
but were identified necessary to ensure a robust model convergence.
Precise tuning of the model circulated around computational efficiency
and model performance, which took considerable time effects.

U-net-based

U-net architecture chosen for the generator proceedings improved the

generator

for extraction of spatial domain features, particularly the color and contrast

spatial

and factors. With the extraction of frequency domain features (using FFT-

frequency domain based technique) further refined the texture and detail restoration.
image
processing

feature Additionally, in this phase, the augmentation techniques impacted the
generalization of the model across diverse low-light conditions, as the
choice and limit of data augmentations significantly impacted training
efficiency, as applying over-the-limit of the desired increased noise in

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

XXIX

AMGAN

APPENDIX D

the training data, while the selected transformations per image produced
more reliable results. Thereby, the phase revealed the importance of
balancing transformation (i.e. augmentations) and training resources in
achieving effectively better convergence.
Dual

Markov With the utilization of dual Markov discriminator, rather than a

discriminator for conventional discriminator technique, the evaluation of both global and
global and local local image aspects was enabled. Leading towards enhanced detail
discrimination

recognition and sharpness, the local discriminator focused on the fine
details such as edges and textures, while the global aspect captures the
large-scale

structures

(i.e.

whole

image).

However,

through

prototyping, it was identified that this setup increased the computation
demands, which resulted in longer training times, and the requirement
of handling overfitting, especially in patches of local regions.
Additionally, regularization techniques (i.e. weight decay, dropout) too
were utilized alongside augmentation, in mitigating overfitting, while
maintaining strong detail levels in the output.
Complete

GAN Integration of the CLSN and GAN architectures at the input level of the

integration

with GAN led to a more balanced enhancement in factors as brightness,

CLSN

texture, color refinement. The U-net-based generator with additional
PatchGAN-based discrimination delivered reasonable results, though
the training process remained at a considerable resource-intensive and
slow-to-converge arena. The ability of the model to generalize across
diverse lighting (of which that includes non-uniform lighting scenarios)
conditions were validated, with requirements to cater the improvement
window.

Data

challenges During the prototyping phase, the inadequacy of targeted and

and

data established low-light image datasets (specifically to handle edge

preprocessing

scenarios such as non-uniform lighting) posed a considerable challenge.
As either the available datasets were restricted for usage, or the open
repositories were not up to expectancies. Therefore, the technique of
filtering the open data repositories based on relevancy were utilized as
the technique. Moreover, image resolution scaling, normalizing based
on

diverse

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

techniques,

based

on

suitability,

application

of

XXX

AMGAN

APPENDIX D

augmentations had to be carefully tuned for assurance in computational
feasibility, while securing model accuracy. Therefore, balancing data
pre-processing steps in current landscape is identified crucial to avoid
unintended complexity on the system during training, while
subsequently enabling data diversity ensuring generalization in realworld low-light scenarios.

E.2 Data flow diagrams
While data flow diagrams are not within the OOADM paradigm (belongs to the SSADM
paradigm), the author was able to provide them as a supplementary effort to dignify the work.
The author has opted to choose ‘Gane & Sarson’ for the data flow diagrams, thereby ensuring
consistency and clarity in representing the processes of the system. The diagrams illustrate how
the data flows between the system-related external entities, components, and data storage.
•

Level 0 (Context diagram): A high-level outline of system interactions with external
entities, which is detailed in Chapter 02.

•

Level 1 (System overview): Demonstrates the interactions between the primary system
components and the data storage compartments of AMGAN.

•

Level 2 (Detailed component view): Provides an in-depth view of image data processing
and component-level interactions executed internally.

APPENDIX F
F.1 Development framework
Development Justification for the selection
framework
PyTorch

PyTorch was selected as the primary deep learning framework, driving
consideration to the dynamic computation graph, ease of debugging, and the
ability to access GPU accelerated resources, thereby increasing overall
efficiency. As it is widely used for research and experimentation, is
represented as an ideal choice for implementing the GAN-based
enhancement model.

Flask

Flask was selected as the web development framework due to the lightweight nature and ease of setting up the APIs, thereby enabling seamless
integration of the trained model into the web-based interface, for a singleclick enhancement to the user, while avoiding overhead to the implementor
of the system.
Table 57: Selection of development framework.

With this selection for the development frameworks, scalability and efficiency are ensured for
both the model training and deployment of the proposed AMGAN system.

F.3.1 Frontend development
As for the front of the application, the web-based UI designed using HTML, CSS, JavaScript,
and Tailwind CSS enables the user to upload low-light images, choose between CLSN-based
brightness enhancement or full enhancement with CLSN and GAN, and download the
enhanced output. The UI elements include:
•

File upload form: The user can select an image to proceed with for the enhancement.

•

Model selection tabs: Provides options between the CLSN and CLSN+GAN models.

•

Image comparison display: Presents the input low-light image and the enhancement.

•

Download option: Gives the user the ability to save the enhancement produced.

•

Project information: Details on the research gaps, objectives, and the expected outcomes.

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

LII

AMGAN

APPENDIX F

F.3.2 Backend integration
The backend is implemented using Flask, which thereby handles the requests for specific image
enhancement phases split between the model selection choices. The frontend sends the
degraded image input to the system to the Flask server, and with the selected model choice,
CLSN or CLSN+GAN, the system processes the image and returns the enhancement result.
API workflow is as follows;
1. The user uploads an image through the form presented on the frontend of the application.
2. The selected model is together sent as a parameter to the Flask backend.
3. The Flask API processes the image with the trained model on checkpoints bearing weights.
4. The enhanced image is returned back to the frontend and is displayed alongside the input.
5. User will now be allowed to download the enhancement produced.
F.3.3 Accessibility considerations
As to ensure a smooth and reliable user experience, the UI follows accessibility guidelines
presented in the table as,

APPENDIX G

APPENDIX G
G.1 Non-functional testing
G.1.1 Performance testing
The performance of the system was assessed based on several key factors with relevance to the
implementation of the proposed system. The considerations were around system
responsiveness, inference time, and computational efficiency. Since the implementation was
executed on a Google Colab environment, at a stage, GPU availability played a distinct role in
processing time efficiency. The model demonstrated stable inference times, where the
enhancement process of degraded to the well-illuminated image was completed within an
acceptable range presented in real-time applications. However, processing higher-resolution
images, as expected, led to increased latency due to the higher tensor weights, which
streamlines the fact that it represents the expected computation demands of a GAN-based
enhancement network model.
Due to this foreseen observation, in the training phase, extended GAN sessions led to session
timeouts, which required implementing checkpoint strategies to enforce training without data
loss. The CLSN module, being a lightweight module, processed the low-light images
efficiently while adjusting the brightness of the image adaptively, as required. The multi-scale
feature extraction in the GAN contributed to the enhancements that were of high quality in
aspects preserving detail, texture, and naturalness of the image but at a higher computational
space, especially directly proportional to the dataset size.
Overall, the system exceeded the expectations of catering to the issue of resolving overlooked
factors in the enhancement stage while balancing the efficiency and quality of enhancement at
a valid state. In proceeding ahead, reduced inference times for higher resolution images and
model quantization techniques (converting high-precision weights to lower precision weights)
to improve the efficiency running on resource-constrained environments are notable areas.
Herewith attached are the browser (Google Chrome/ MS Edge) developer tools performance
profiling results, which analyze the efficiency reached in executing the frontend of the
application, the rendering time of the application, and the JavaScript processing overhead
reached.

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

LVI

AMGAN

APPENDIX G

Figure 37: Performance testing - browser results (self-composed).

To ensure the accessibility and responsiveness of the developed web application for the
proposed system when rendered across various devices and screen sizes, the author has
proceeded with compatibility testing using the browser tools. The application was designed
with a flexible and responsive UI, thereby enabling the application to adapt dynamically based
on the different screen resolutions and varying aspect ratios between device categories.
The developer tools embedded within the native browsers were utilized to simulate the different
devices and to proceed with the evaluation of the renderings and the responsiveness, layout
spanning, consistency, and, most importantly, component scaling. Ranging from the various

H.2 Remainder of self-evaluations
Theme

Evaluation by the author

Limitations

The primary technical limitation of this research resonates upon the

and

future computational requirements of the GAN-based architecture, complemented

enhancements by another reinforcement branch, which in combination, demands high-end
GPUs for training and inference. While the optimizations were applied to
cater the challenge, further model compression techniques, such as
knowledge distillation could be explored for targeting on-device application
for edge-devices. Another potential area in the qualitative sphere is to
improve the naturalness across distinct environments, and the utilization of
self-supervised techniques for avoiding the dependency on large, labeled
datasets. Despite these challenges, the research was successfully established
with a strong foundation for further advancements in dual-domain and
efficient adaptive enhancement with deep learning based LLIE.
Table 62: Remainder of self-evaluations.

H.5.3 System design and architectural effectiveness
Code Evaluation
Domain and Technical Experts (ML/DL/CV/IP/GANs/CNN-driven expertise)
EV1

“You don’t need to worry, just go ahead and explain it clearly. Keep it compact and
show what impact it has. Your approach is going to help. Some people may question
it, yet as long as it is well-structured and explained, it’s good. From a system design
perspective, it is structured well. If you are planning for a real-time system, then you
need to consider whether it can run on a mobile device or if it requires highperformance hardware. If you can make it run without a GPU, how much memory
does it consume? How big is the model? All of these factors should be considered
and documented. The design is well thought out, and as long as it is structures
properly, it should work effectively.”

EV2

“I think the proposed architecture is effective because, in research, it is not just about
the performance gains but also about considering the available resources. Given the
resource constraints, this is the most effective and best model that could be
developed for this problem. The system is well-structured because you have done
the research beforehand and learned from previous work. You have come up with a
new architectural framework that directly addresses this problem, which is an
impressive outcome for this timeframe.”

EV3

“I think the architecture is very effective. On a scale of 1 to 10, I would rate it a 9.
You are using a U-Net structure, which seems very efficient, and I think you have
chosen a strong approach. Your architecture is complex because you are joining two
models together, which adds substantial depth to the methodology. One suggestion
for improvement would be to train both models in a single training flow rather than
separately, in an end-to-end process rather than training them separately. An
integrated training flow would differentiate.”

EV4

“The architecture is well-designed to tackle the non-uniform low-light enhancement
problem. The CLSN block focuses on feature extraction and inverse grey map
computation, while the GAN block refines the output with frequency domain
processing. The use of a GAN-based discriminator ensures realistic image

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

XCIII

AMGAN

APPENDIX H

reconstruction. The benchmark results confirm that the architecture can enhance
low-light images more effectively than some prior approaches.”
EV5

“I find your architecture very cool and innovative, but it might not be immediately
understandable to non-technical users. If you plan to extend this as a business
solution, don’t stop here, try to take it further. One suggestion is to educate the user
on how the image enhancement process works. You can deploy step-by-step
transformations to help users to understand what’s happening behind the scenes. This
transparency would make the system more effective and help gain user trust.”

EV6

“GANs and Deep Convolutional Neural Networks are commonly used to improve
low-light images. This hybrid approach is novel and effective because it integrates
both spatial and frequency-based features and use the advantages of both domains.
The results given are also competitive and proves the effectiveness.”

EV7

The problem of non-uniform lighting in LLIE is critical, as many methods tend to
overexpose bright areas while attempting to enhance darker ones. This method
accompanies inverse gray maps as adaptive attention mechanism seems to be an
effective way to target local contrasts dynamically. The multi-scale learning
approach ensures that both of global contrast and fine textures are maintained. Since

H.6 User-study findings

enhancement methods alongside the proposed method results. They were given a score on a
scale of 1 to 5, and whichever the highest scored out of the below mentioned samples were
chosen as the best. A total of 41 users scorings were received.

APPENDIX I

I.3 Achievement of learning outcomes
Description

Learning
outcome(s)

The project was into two submodules as the CLSN-based inverse grey LO1
attention map enhancement and GAN-based enhancement. These were further
stretched into atomic units to tackle and implement step-by-step. Appropriate
techniques were selected based on the literature survey and expert feedback to
apply progressively in the implementation.
A Gantt chart was created to map the tasks, track the progress, and to ensure LO2
the timely delivery of them, within the defined timeline. Priority was
distributed across tasks and milestones were monitored regularly.
Requirements were gathered through the domain and technical experts, LO3
utilizing interviews, problem domain exploration, and literature sources. These
helped the identification of core limitations in LLIE, targeting ever existing
non-uniformity issues and defined the enhancement goals, accordingly.
Extensive literature was reviewed based around GANs, Retinex-based LO4
methods, U-Net, Residual Networks, CLSN mechanism, and frequency
domain techniques such as FFT. This guided the designing of the hybrid
enhancement architecture, through the identified potential and requirements.
With the completion of initial insight gathering, the project was planned LO5, LO6,
modularly, with each phase, from pre-processing to final model deployment, LO7
was executed independently and was validated through rigorous iterations.
Regular meeting with the project supervisor ameliorated the alignment of the
deliverables with the desired expectations.
All documentation was prepared based on iterative and frequent feedback LO8
received. The final report included the critical reflections on the requirement
elicitations, methodology, implementation, testing, and results, while the
document artefacts, as the project proposal, literature review, project proposal
and requirement specification (PPRS), and interim progress demonstration
(IPD), were submitted in due time to ensure the success of the project.
Furthermore, the author submitted four papers, including two survey papers,

Pansilu Wijesiri | w19127880

CXXVII

AMGAN

APPENDIX I

an extended abstract, and a research paper to solidify the research. It also
demonstrated the learning curve and overall contribution.
The project was demonstrated with a live system application interface and was LO9
successfully defended during the viva examination, backed up by the model
results explained and justified clearly and comprehensively.
Table 77: Achievement of learning outcomes.

↑ Back to main content ↑

I.4 Technical/ additional contributions
•

Developed a functional, end-to-end LLIE system based on a web-based GUI that supports
system interactions, real-time enhancement, output comparison, and access to benchmark
models trained specifically over SOTA dataset variations.

•

Implemented the training pipelines modularly for both CLSN and GAN components,
thereby ensuring future extensibility and adaptability to other enhancement tasks and
domains.

•

Demonstrated the practical deployment feasibility of the proposed LLIE solution by
achieving SOTA-level performance under distinct lighting conditions.

APPENDIX J

APPENDIX J
J.1 Key steps involved in the CLSN enhancement process
Stage

Description

Extraction

of The generation of inverse grey maps involves the process of utilizing

image channel details from each channel features, thereby craving for deep feature
features

for extraction, while retaining the original feature distributions of the degraded

generating
inverse

image. To meet such a requirement, the CNN is accompanied by a U-Net,
grey where the down sampling and up sampling process with skip connections

map

maintains the minute information through applying filters throughout the
U-shaped architecture, benefitted from the resolutions with diverse
receptive fields, with capturing features from different scales as finer
details in the earlier layers, and more abstract features from the deeper
layers, thereby retrieving low-light image information at diverse levels of
granularity.

Inverse

grey The CLSN produces a final inverse gray map utilizing the grey maps from

map generation each color channel (R, G, B) with the U-Net architecture. The U-Net
resonated on the capabilities in capturing the spatial hierarchies, thereby
retrieving details from both dark and bright regions of the degraded image.
These inverse grey maps assign higher grey values to dark areas while the
vice-versa to the well-illuminated areas.
Concatenation

With the presence of inverse grey maps for each channel, they are

with

the concatenated together to form a one unified inverse grey map, and then is

original

low- the resulting inverse grey map is then concatenated with the degraded low-

light image

light image input. This process guides the model to focus on the valid
distribution of brightness factor, as to focus on underexposed regions
without leaning towards overexposed regions within the image.
Table 78: Key steps involved in the CLSN enhancement process.
